O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the latest of medical knowledge along with its completion, and I have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to my mind that I would complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is neglected in our region and is despised everywhere, it has been lost and cut off, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that have been written by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off, and knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	I think it seems to me that I want to bring to life together the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will bring together the forms of cauterizing instruments and other tools for this work with the adjustment of their declaration and preparation as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because of this reason that no good master surgeons are found in our time, the art of medicine is distant.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes it to know anatomy, as Galen says, so long as he knows the joints of the members, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of them, and their location and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And therefore says Hippocrates that a name with a name is much, but with the work is little.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the introduction to this book that whoever is not knowledgeable of the things before mentioned should beware lest they stumble in error and harm people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	in so far as I have wished many times to warn those who take part in this art and abandon their science and sense of experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I have seen a foolish surgeon who cut off the abscess from the scrofulous neck of a woman and cut the arteries of the neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Why so much blood flows out that the woman fell dead between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And we have seen another man who treated a stone from an old man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man inside died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the great size of the stone, and I knew well that if it was not removed he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And we have seen another surgeon who treated the leg of a duke from our land which was broken, and with the break there was a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the ignorant surgeon held the break above the wound with stitches by strong thread, and did not leave any linen on the wound at all, and thus left him to his end;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded that it not be undone.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and thus it remained so that the leg was completely inflamed and the feet came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I am summoned to come to him, and I hurry to come to free his leg.
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I loosen it so that it is at peace and he feels no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the same the corruption had already taken hold in the member, and I could not heal it;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the whole limb was completely destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I have seen another surgeon who opened up an infected abscess, and then inflamed it through his own ineptitude.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	When a chancre is pure of melancholic humour, it does not require iron to be touched if it is in such a place that everything corrupted can be removed from it.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, very dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two sections:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work in which there is danger in many conditions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show you in each place of this book where it has fear and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Why it is necessary for you to guard against it, so that the foolish observer cannot speak badly of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take up your arms in custody, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and employ the best method so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and let the troublesome diseases of bad sanitation;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and put down your arms from those things that make you doubt, and have courage in yourselves so that you can come to the other world of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galien says in one of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take on a sick patient who will call you a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have written this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are of fire cauteries and of hot medical cauteries, and the chapter is ordered from head to feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the shapes of instruments, and of iron clamps for cautery, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and of poultices and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it deals with the ordering and shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it deals with the ordering of instruments from head to foot, and the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, so that we remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of aid and harm in each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the quality of healing, and the cause of harm, is the longest talk and subtlest science and secret responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and many wise people spoke about this, and agreed with it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I shorten their words for they are too long because I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cauterizing helps universally to every temperament where there is matter, except for two temperaments:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	it is to know hot constitution with cold matter, and dry constitution with cold matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry constitution together with cold matter, they decided one thing and said that cautery is great aid;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the other said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is not worth for illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure a hot illness with heat, nor by dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he who said the opposite says that cautery does great aid for a hot and dry illness that comes in the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true at some point through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any way, do not interfere with those who have proved it, and who know by long experience the chapter of cauterizations, and the diversity of constitutions of men, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the cures and the time when.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	we have no fear of other constitutions, especially in cold and wet diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the wise men gathered together and agreed on cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that combined fire is a secret of cures and of greater goodness than burning medical cauterization.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	Because the fire is simple, and it doesn't harm any other member if its name is not known; and it only harms the burned part.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	hot remedies come from member to member, causing and bringing grievous sicknesses of difficult recovery to the affected limb.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and it may happen that the patient dies.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	the fire on account of its greatness and because of the goodness of its substance does not cause harm, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And I have found this for you through experience and the length of my service and study that I have put into the art, and it was based on a true understanding of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this reason I excuse the length of my words, because it displeases me to take from you the secret which is resolved by fire and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Or you receive them in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on the timing of when cauterizations should be done and selected certain patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is advisable at all times, because the evil growths beneath are put to rights by the aid of cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and above all if the cauteries are for urgent pains that cannot wait until a greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think this, dear son, as foolish men do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cautery has no relapse.
et il le dient ensi;	and they say so themselves;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not so as they think, for cautery is not but a medicine that moves the complexion and dries the humors which are the cause of pain, and avails more than other medicines in hastening its value and virtue through the efficacy and power of its work.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	It is possible that the disease will come upon the patient at some time according to the temperament of the patient and the location of the disease itself.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and the excesses are gathered in him from the acquisition of meats and similar things, unless there are cauterizations administered to the place where he has an excess of superfluity and moisture, such as a burning on the pain, and similar things, and that pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this is rare.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and that is true.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterizations are worth after medicine, but their intention is false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of treatment in some illness and they are not effective, then we administer cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	So now you understand well that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not as foolish men think.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancient ones said that cauters made of golden instrument are more effective than those made of iron, and they did not say this because of the quality of gold but because of its high density.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the places of cauterization do not become infected, but this is not true for I have tried it and found that it is so in some men.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and golden cauters are worth more than iron ones, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And anyway when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know whether it is heated or not by the color of the gold, and it cools down immediately.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	they put it in fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use cauterization made of iron, because it has been proven suitable to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have written out this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that it will be easier for you to find what you need.
dou cautere olivaire	The chapter on oil cauterization.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These oil cauterizations are effective against moisture and cold in the head, and there are two types of them: one is done because of a disease called "soda", and another because of many humors that descend from the head to the ears, and for a multitude of headaches, toothaches, and throat pain, as well as all diseases that come from coldness, such as paralysis, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar maladies.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a medicinal solution softening the head to three or four parts, according as the virtues and age and habit of the patient can suffer.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make him recline his head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit with his arms crossed between your hands, and place his hands on the balance scale.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	place the root of your palm on the root of his navel between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and when it comes to your middle fingers, if it bleeds in the center then heat the cauterizer which is called "olivare", of which this is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and move your hand downwards and outwards in a twisting motion;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand straight up, and return to the spot if you see the bone itself clearly small;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, then reheat the cauterizer until you see the bone as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	after that take a piece of cloth and wet it and make it soft with cotton inside, and place it on the spot, and let it be for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	after putting a wet cloth soaked in lard on the spot;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it there until the heat is gone.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treating the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmacion", so long as it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	and they said that the older ones, that the longer an open wound stays, the cleaner it becomes.
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason does not help much.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that the cauterization should be done so thoroughly that part of the bone is burned, and then once what has been burned of the bone is scraped off, it should be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And they say the other that one should let the cautery burn so much on it, and press so hard that you lower to the bone as wide as the strip that women put in their armpits because the humors run out there.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one should leave the wound open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after that one should treat and bind it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem to me at all good in every case, except for some men where there is a way of fear.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I must let it go;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the joint is weakened by continuous flowing of nature, as we witness in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and similarly when the joint of the patient is weak by nature, and the first sign of cauterizing is more safe and better for me, and from that I work in such a way as to bring about safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	The ancient pain of the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When in the whole head there comes chronic pain and it lasts for a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie", and purgatives of the head and oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one does to him the cauterization that we have said before, and it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take note if the joint of the patient is of hot nature, and is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Then apply a fire cauterization below it, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards make a fire cauterization on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make another cauterization at the place which is called "vasselz".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the place where one puts cups.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and stretch out your hand so that you do not see up to the bone.
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels too much greater pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and the cauterizers for the horns should be finer than those by which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and that is the form;
dou cautere dou chief	The cauterization of the head.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes to one part of the head and the disease is spread as far as the eye and the joints are purged by cleansing medicines and all the other cures that I have said in the division of diseases have been done, and none of it helps.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then he makes cauterizations according to two manners, namely of hot water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	the cauterizations of hot water are such that you take a sweet wine and remove the crust and recollect it to two handfuls, and then make the temple where the pain is, in such a manner that you can place the sweet wine beneath the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it has been reapplied, tie and bind it tightly and leave it thus for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then untie him and treat the wound with garlic wine, and let the wound remain thus two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put on a poultice dipped in butter as long as there be pus issuing from it.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	Afterward, anoint with ointment until he is healed.
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you wish to do the recipe of some constricting medicines that I have written or in the twelfth book treat on constraining medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is performed in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery so that it takes this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clos" because the head is shaped like a bell or a horn, and in the middle it has a small appearance.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and put it on the painful place and hold your hand and twist the iron a little bit until the middle of the splinter is burnt.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand that the artery does not burn, because it lies outside, and a great abundance of blood flows out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Then put cotton in a linen cloth, and place it on the place for three days.
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then I put moistened cotton in butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "culter", all over the tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this migraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	The migraine.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you cure a migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not profit, and you see that the fire cauterization which we spoke of earlier does not help him, then it is necessary that you heat the cauterizer which is called "cultellare" until it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and then sign on the painful spot a line of half a thumb's length deep, and remove your hand once, and keep from covering the artery and proceed just to the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the jaw that moves when it is touched, and the nerve has regard only for the mouth and spasms do not come to the patient, and beware of the cutting of the artery's blood when it is cut, or a great fear comes upon it even to him who does not know, and who is not experienced or tried.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the work proceed along my way;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop blood when an artery is cut, and I will show you at the place where it is written in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauterizations do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize also on the head as we have said, and heal the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cauterization which we have said in the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with a cauterizer that has two knives;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cauterizer is better and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	The pain in the ears from coldness.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from coldness, and all sorts of purging medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division have been tried without success, then heat this cauterizing instrument called "poins", whose form is:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	Then pierce all around the ailing ear, or around both if the pain holds in both, and draw aside a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place for incision.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and has it placed with X points around each ear.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure, let it be in place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	The torment of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	The torture that should be cured by cauterizing is not other than those that move due to flux, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not make a cauterization on appearances that come from evil and splenic humors.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this appearance of torture that moves due to yellow bile and purging of the head and gargarism, and it does not work, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauterizations.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one in the root of the ear, and the other a spot behind the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cauterizer in the part that appears healthy, and make a cauterization right next to the ear of the head on a spot beneath the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as one finger.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and let the cautery be applied so high that the middle of the skin is burned.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the scalpel that we have placed in front, but it is a bit more subtle and it must be that the knife is a bit larger.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure leave the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you treat it in this way as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauterizations:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one on the place that is called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and it should be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	Litargy.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	To this sickness it is necessary to give the patient great year-old apples and mind-clearing pills.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After removing the king's (hair) from the head of the patient, and putting a mustard plaster on the back of the head which is written in the treatise about plasters.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the method of cauterizing;
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do it as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is cleansed in this way, it is well.
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not cleansed, then you do three cauterizations between the head and the neck, and have two large figs in between each cauterization.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and you treat him as the others, and if it appears to be festering and the patient is suffering, then you do one cauterization in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, two others on the two horns, and you treat him until he is cleansed.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and there is a fire cautery called "olivar", as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	The coldness of the head.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of years and of what we have spoken about before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after rinsing the patient's head, then make a cautery on the head and above each horn, and in the rear and three times on the spine of the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you have more need of it, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is fierce, make four cauterizations on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave it until the utmost cure be burned, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the cure is complete, and be the cautery called "olivar" that we have spoken of before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy.
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should only use cauterization if they are phlegmatic, and it is first necessary to purge the brain with years and other remedies that we have said in the section on great and suffering patients.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot suffer it, make him gurgle and chew a cleansing of the brain often with good meats.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king's crown is cut off, and there is a fire cautery as we have said before, and the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is severe and suffering, make fire cauterizations as I said to one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and the olive oil cautery according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, then do 1 subtle cauterization in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy the superfluities or moistures are corrupted and phlegm is thick, then do the cauterization with many cauters as we have said to someone who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy the superfluities decline into melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give them to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to what we have said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king's crown of the patient.
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	Make a linen compress well made, also like a bandage, and put it on the head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	And the patient should be crossed over [himself], and held tight from all parts.
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After present the poultice, and worth a move of elder tree cream.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	And the hot water tempered with fire, so that the patient can bear to have it applied.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	After emptying the circle within the head, and letting it cool.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and have this patient do this each week once with another good treatment, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you wish to cauterize an area, make several small points all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery moistens the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on damp cotton in lard and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	de la auge ou du sel de l'œil
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye disease comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then start and give the patient to drink something purifying the head, and keep him away from all moisture, and make him sweat or take several baths at fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Then command him to turn back his head, and have him cauterized in the head, and have two cauterizations on the two temples if the descent of the humour is to both eyes together, or in one eye.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cover all the cauterized places with veins and arteries that are under the skull, and have the cauterization long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and be careful about bloodletting, and if you see too much blood come out, stop it with all the power that you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and at the incision, the cautery, how to stretch it out.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and whenever we have done a cautery or cauterization beneath the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the tears of the body
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When tears from the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear in the appearance of the head outside.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that it is a cold humid superfluity, then the doctor makes the cautery which I said at the beginning of this chapter descending to the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I make a cautery in the head, and two cauterizations on the two temples, and two cauterizations or cauterisms beneath the two bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if it is necessary to do more, then bleed him with a cautery above the knot in little pieces.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	from within the body through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	If you give medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit him, then give the patient three cups of broth.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king has been treated, and the head has been cauterized with oil of olive cautery.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauters of the "clavilis" cautery on the two eyebrows, a little below the nose.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery so that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And that is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see, make two cauters on the two eyebrows just as long as the eyelashes are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave your hand there unless the third part of the paper is burnt, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	two hairs which prick the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyelashes are converted to beards, and they prick the eye, and one makes cauters in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	it is to know of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	Or cautery with fire instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they have grown and are even, then put the patient in a warm bath;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	afterwards draw on paper the shape of the eyes as a leaf of myrtle is, and that is the beginning of the sign near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then I put moist cotton on an egg white and musk-like mixture of purslane over the eye, then heat the cautery so that this is its shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	Afterwards cauterize on the figure that you have drawn a little at a time and with little touches, so that the kernels are burned right there;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of health of the work are that you see the paper [? possibly "scar tissue" or "flesh"] drawn back, and the hairs raised at the tip of the eye.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then lift your hand, and let it be so for three days; then put moistened cotton in a poultice until the swelling is gone.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the ointment treatment as long as they are healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after that the hairs come back and the scar tissue becomes softened then resume the cautery over that same place just as you did first.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs have gone away, then cauterize so that the scar tissue is raised to its natural place and is even, and does not prick at the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The burning cauterization of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow as long and even as possible, then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and fresh gall from each one a third, and crush them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then apply it to the shape that you have made like the leaf of the myrtle tree, and put on paper over the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease lies only in one place, then it should be worked on that one, and both of them as well;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put wet cotton under the eye;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the patient's head is in good health and put your finger showing above the medicine, and press the pot and the egg all the times that the patient feels pain from the medicine, for he feels a stinging as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine with your thumb. (Note: This is likely a step to stop the burning sensation of the cauterization)
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the stinging has passed, then lift up the paper cloth, and reward yourself if you see the paper lifted in the same way as if it had been lifted by force of fire or by an incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is thus, so be it.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, he should apply more medicine to the place or where the medicine has no effect, until your tasks are equal and your eyes are in order.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on moistened cotton in a burr until the hot iron is cooled, after that clean the place of the ointment which is called "diaphenies" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to be careful with your work so that the medicine does not come into contact with your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards and the hairs prick in the eye, then reapply the medicine to that place which has become softened with clean paper properly, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after that cure until it is healed.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the shape of a mulberry leaf.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and in smallness, and according to those will be your constraints.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and the right path is not shown to him who has the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of a fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure fistulas as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is fitting that you make them cauterize according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	instruct the patient to put his head under a tub or vat.
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and have the servant hold the patient's head between their hands in such a manner that it does not move, nor lean back.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then place moist cotton on the eye socket or on the juice of parsley over the eye.
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after that heat the cautery which is such:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and shape it to the head like a feather of a goose, together with its quill being the cautery.
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if it is seen, if it is pointed from one end to the other, and if it is seen, then also like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but however, this which is shaped is worth more for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing on the fistula it becomes open, and you draw out the pus, and dry it.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, do the operation, and draw out the boil outside;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	After place the hot cautery form on it, and hold your hand over the cautery at the part near to the eye above; so that your hands do not make foolishness.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery in the fatty part of the eye and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then repeat the cautery again once more, and another if you need it, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After I place moistened cotton in butter, and apply the ointment of drying until they are healed, and if forty days have passed that they are not healed, then apply caustic medicine until the bone is uncovered.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the king according to whatever he came in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand that it is a fistula, and clean out the place.
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after put in the cut a subtle Camphan to which this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they make it to the quantity of a little quarter of a plum;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand or Camphan firmly, and do not let the patient move until the melted plum runs to his oil;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary that you put on the oil of the patient a moistened cotton or in an eggshell or in an awl;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the plum if it closes the place of the fistula and the wound heals by wonderful medicine.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed through the cauterization that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer pertain to the neck, and bring the fistula back to its proper place in the neck.
des crevaices en levres	cold sores on the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times happen cracks in the lips that are called "furcule", and even in the children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you care for these cracks in the manner that we have said in sections, and the care does not help, then sharpen a small cauterizing tool according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	and put it hastily in those cracks until it comes to a point (or becomes solid).
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after, heal the place with wax until it is sound.
de l’aposteme de la goule	a swelling in the throat (or a goiter)
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes to the root of the jaw or in the eyelid, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it forms a foul-smelling discharge and becomes festering and turns into a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in sections, but it does not benefit.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you make the fire cautery according to the size of the fistula.
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening or hole of the fistula, hold your hand so that the iron becomes hot to the point where it comes out at the end.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this once or twice, after treating what we have said in treatments, until they are healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is treated thus, it is good.
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of toothache (due to movement of teeth)
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine and this is not effective, then put the patient's head in your saliva.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heating the cautery the form will come out like this afterwards you place a stick on the tooth.
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put the hot cautery inside and hold it so long that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after lift your hand and start the cautery again according to your will.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after fill the patient's mouth with salted water, and let it stand for an hour and a rich sweat.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the tooth that was moving is congealed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupted moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache (dolor des dens)
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain comes from cold or hot and the cures of medicine are not worth it, then there is need for a cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and a poultice of butter and a fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	A poultice of butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and the bottom in a spoon of iron or of tin.
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent, and soak it in melted butter, and put it on the aching tooth hastily and keep it until it cools down.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and so do it often until the virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that a woolen and cotton poultice in cold butter, and put on the aching tooth, and put on hot iron until fire comes to the cheekbone of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cauterization together is such that you take a dog of iron or tin, and it should be thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After the heating of the cautery, whose shape will come to be here afterwards, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next at most.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good butter in pressing on that cautery, and then let it drip.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery on whatever part of the head you want, and according to your ability;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the shape of the cordial.
des scrophules	Of swellings.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrofula are of bad humors and cold moisture, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery shaped like this which comes next, and make two openings so that the fumes may come out at the other part.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and put the hot cauterization on the abscess once, or as often as is necessary, until it reaches the depth of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small put a cauterization according to the size of the abscess, and leave it so for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put on moistened cotton in butter until the scab is removed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after that treat the place with ointments and dressings until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the dog's body:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the humors overcome on the channels of the womb, and even when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first with soluble medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	after that do a cauterization at the root of the throat, and be careful not to come close to the throat, and don't let it burn too much but just a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After making another cautery at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and let the cautery be which is called "clavicle" of which we have the form before.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal the place as we have said before until it is cured.
de la toust	Il semble que nous avons changé de sujet ! La toust est un type de petit pain croustillant, typiquement français. Est-ce que vous voulez discuter des recettes de toust ou quelque chose d'autre ?
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all the diseases of the groin are from cold moistures, and the patient has neither fever nor heat, and it is an old disease, then make two cauteries on the inguinal region in front.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery inside the breast between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery be which is called "clavicle" according to the form said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, make a cautery in pricking to the whole cautery which is called "point" of which the form is shown above in the disease of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the hairs grow to a length of thirty or thereabouts.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After healing the place according to what is said above, and the cautery is applied at III reins according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And therefore are the cauteries more gentle, because you make three on a stick.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the shoulder joint is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Then have the patient be anointed with something on his back and chest.
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then lift up the kerf that is inside the titillite in the direction of the left hand from your right.
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inside, then warm up the cauterizer that has two needles pointed like this.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the kerf until it pierces to the chest, and come out four times with the fumes of the cauterizer together.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and therefore the cautery is made with the cauterizer that has three needles, so that there are six figures of cauterization.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent and it is the shape of the cauterizer that has three needles:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And never once is added on top of this one thread, for which reason there are eight marks of cauterization.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After put on the cautery powder mixed with linen;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after let the patient rest and do not move the limbs for a long time until he is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, such a thing occurs frequently, then make a cautery over the thick part of the cautery needle, or many cauterers that are pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is reformed, and the moisture is dried up, and the patient's wound is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come into the stomach, and they hold him back from his complexion, and many purgings occur in him, and by accustomed cures he does not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Then after that make him three cauterizations: one under the rib of the back as long as an egg, with all the cautery sharpened, and two cauterizations on both sides so that the figure of the cauterization is at three angles, and have such space between one and the other that they are not joined together when they suppurate.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauterizations be so deep that they reach the two parts of the bone, and let the figure of the cauterizations be according to this shape without junction:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see a need to cauterize with a great cautery in the stomach according to this shape;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who has fear of this cautery, shall be cauterized in pricking and marked above the stomach at a point according to the quantity that you see of gall;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then burn him with the entire cautery called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the wound that we have had before, until they are healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When pain from cold and moisture and thick biliousness comes to the liver, so that it is excessively changed from its natural complexion by excesses.
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured from what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him, so it is necessary that the patient be warned on his heart.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and mark a gallbladder with three cauters according to this form and shape and quantity above the liver, beyond the navel, where the hips of the man come.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and let there be an interval between each cauter of the thickness of a thumb.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	And they are to apply the cauterization long on the body; and do not press very tightly with your hand at all the cauterization.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and it is to be burned only as much of the skin as suffices; and the patient is to sit upright on his feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, so let him lean back, and stretch out his legs, and lift up his arms.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the shape:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you wish, then cauterize these cauters with a knife, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn all the skin, for you would dry out the whole body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let it not come as soon as possible, for the skin is very tender at that place, and you know well enough to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When he has an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too strongly.
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the tendon, he feels a sharp pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment was done by the midwives, it was necessary for the patient to be laid on her back on a bed.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then mark the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a reed, of which this is the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And with the cautery burn until the core is burned and comes to a black boil, as long as the pustule is completely purged.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment according to the treatment of abscesses as long as it is healed.
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not necessary that any other sores arise from this cautery except those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have cured at some time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly work on it, and yet to me it seems that it is better to let him alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The old men said that one must make fire cauterizations for pleurisy with roots of aristologia, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	take a root of aristologia as long as you can find, and be dry, and also thick and also long as your thumb;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and soak it in oil, and take hold of it to the fire, and cauterize one cauterization between the sternum and the neck, and two small cauterizations a little below in the part that is under the beard;
