et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauterizations between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining behind a little bit;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cauterization in the chest, and another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two at both sides of the chest below the cauterization that is between the two shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press your hand at all, rather make it open as when smelling;
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	They said that an old man used to apply a fire cautery resembling a razor, and he would warm it up and put it between the ribs, until it came to the abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and it would bring relief from pain, just as we have said in a case of liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear for the patient's death now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! "De la mie" est une expression française qui signifie "du pain" ou "le centre". Est-ce que vous avez une citation ou un texte lié à cela ?
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	Merci pour le contexte ! Il semble que nous ayons affaire à un texte médical ancien.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	One of the methods is that you make three cauterizations, or four, along the length of the swelling, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have said before.
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand on the entire cauterization, and let the patient sit on his back.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another method of cauterization is that you heat the cauterizer which has two handles, as we have shown in the case of shoulder dislocation;
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and lift the cauterizer which is placed over the swelling, or where the patient's chest comes towards his left side, and be sure that the elevations from which you lift the cauterizer are according to the shape of the body, and the cauterizers are according to the breadth of the body.

Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The burning medical cautery is that you make an instrument between the hinges of the door, and it is made of iron or steel with a handle one foot long, and in its height has two nails, and between each there is the quantity of the thickness of a thumb.

Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline substance and hot water, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them into a new pot.

Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés. Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And say in this manner that you take green verdigris fresh and dry, and grind it very well with a peck of fat, and put it on the armpit and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain lies.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and let him lie three hours and by the quantity that the patient feels no more burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then have him enter into a bath until his body is somewhat warmed up, and have him enter into bed, and the pain will go away altogether and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cauterization for such medications, unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's hair fire, it helps a lot.
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and must be done the cautery in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and put it on the hollow between the big toe and the other that is called foscele.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	Then take dry goat's hair and put it to the fire until it is charcoal, and then place it on the skin, and let it stay until it cools.
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and redo it again like that, and do not stop doing so until you think that it will come just up to the groin, and that the pain will cease;
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and this method of cauterization is called "cautery of goat".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or percussion or too great evacuation, or from seeming of cold matter spread out, no one of these appearances is worth cauterizing, except that which comes from infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary afterward that the patient be voided of fetid pills or others similar, and a mixture put on his back, there where the pain holds, marked with three lines of ink, and in each line V cauteries or more according to virtue and quantity that the patient can endure;
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and let the cautery be done according to the cautery which is called "prick".
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see fit, do three cauteries or four at the middle key cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this illness comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have narrow elbows when they move them, and fear;
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you will find in the lower spine of the back and on its appearance which comes up on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it heal, then cauterize at the cautery of the back according to this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If you apply a red hot cautery to each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine with a burning cautery that is 2 or 3 lines long, and the points are close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure has healed as much as it is clean according to what we have said, and beware that you do not bring a cautery near the elbow where there is a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When pain from the joints is due to moisture that spreads throughout each member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which doctors call "podagre" properly, and when it is of cold cause and cures of medicines cannot heal it, then cure it with cauterizations in this manner:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	make a ball of cauterizers around the joint of the foot, and the cauterizer should be olive-like in this shape:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you touch above the face of the foot, then make a cautery all over with the hot cautery that we call "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come just to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, make a cauterizer on each knee three or four of each part, with the whole cauterizer olive-like;
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	and if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand further than until the spines of the cauterizer are burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knee and on the back, administer the cauterization that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are on the hands, make points around the joint 2 lines.
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if pain remains at your shoulder, make points above each joint and above the hair of the hand.
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if pains come as far as the sides or as far as the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and make good management of the patient and apply remedies.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and purge his phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	...the treatment for hernia.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When rupture comes in the navel, and the bowels descend to the genitals and it is new, then you must not let them operate on it that day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and he uses things which loosen the belly, so that the devil descends from his belly.
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	then have him sit on his back between your hands, and command that he stretches his navel so that the intestines are repaired, and you reset them to their place, and give an incision under the rupture above the bone of the elbow, and make a sign like the half of a circle above the body.
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then heat the cauterizing iron whose form is this:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as he remains white and spits up pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then reset the bowels to their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and the servants stain his hand above so that they do not return rearward;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and well bind the thighs of the patient, and put under him a cushion and a servant above the thighs, and another above the chest who holds his hands;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then put the cauterizing iron on the sign above all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat again another time until you go through just to the bone;
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and be wary carefully that the bowel does not burst when you make the cauterizing;
que tu ne le brulasses;	so that you do not burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and that through this the patient does not die, or another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you don't come close to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to their size, and also great for grown people according to their measure;
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days' cure let the place of the cauterized butter be left uncovered as long as the scab is removed;
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after the cure of other ointments until they are healed, and have the patient lie on his back for forty days in order that the wound may be well closed;
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that his sores be left uncovered for a long time, so that the boils may not burst when he will go into bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, have him brought a well-made bandage, and wear it for forty other days;
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and let him have good rest, that he does not exhaust himself too much and be careful to drink and eat too much, and not climb up too high;
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And when he does this teaching, then he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say next the cure of cutting as is written in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When ulcers come to other organs and are recognized, and you see that they no longer grow, then make the fire cauterize according to its quantity, and have it burn a third part of its width.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the cure according to what we said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients have said that one must cauterize with the fire at three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but the first mark indicate the middle of the fistula and make one line above it over the fistula, and another below, and hold your hand in it all along the entire cautery groove.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and less effective.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes into any member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine does not work, then it is necessary that he be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cautery be according to the length of the member, and its tenderness and weakness, and its virtue and its location, and its twistings and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	if he is healed from the first cauterization, it is good.
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	if it is not healed, start another cauterization on top of that one, for this custom is that it must fester in the member that is nearest to it, therefore you should do the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of wound healing (or surgery)
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The members are helped sometimes by cauterization with great effort, and the same disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	Can you not see that it is cauterized, be aware if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that corruption will penetrate all of the patient, then he makes five cauterizations on the head.
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I lower the head to the back, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the cheek.
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and then above the two horns, and it behind above the occiput.
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and let it stay until the cautery comes up to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can issue.
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize on the nose according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the swelling is spread out everywhere;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it visibly declines, then you should cauterize with those cauters that we have said for the head, and one cauter on the neck, and two cauteres on the spine of the neck, and six cauteres on the spine of the back, and one large on the armpit and another nearby, and two on the two shoulders.
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and two [operations] on the shoulders, and two on the tendons of the ribcage, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the joints of the hands.
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and be careful with the nerves that are above the backside of the heel, so as not to burn them;
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and once make a cautery on the bone of the finger, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that whenever you make more cauterization, it is more helpful to the patient, and brings greater benefit;
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	and know that the sick person does not feel pain in the cautery as much as the healthy person feels it, because the body is already quite corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	It is necessary that the cauterizing be large and small according to the members and joints, as you will find it in the manner of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the cure, heal the place with flour a few times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When an inflammation comes to any member and is treated by medicines and oils and plasters, but it is not healed, then make a cautery on the member according to the size and smallness of the member.
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cauterize be a small piece entering into the skin of the cure.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal with ointments until they are healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And at any time when one makes a cauterization and in the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve which moves the limb, and thus if there is inflammation.
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and at all times no one should meddle with it unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	Of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the illness called "albaras" is inflamed, and the medicine does not work for it, then cauterize with a cauterize a piece deep, according to the quantity of the skin of the cure, as long as the swelling is removed, and its color changes.
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then heal with flour of vetches and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of coloquint and blood of almond, each a part.
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and it should be mixed together altogether, and tied with a cloth, and aired at its place as long as it is clean.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil comes at the beginning and you stop up the view, if one cauterizes with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the boil.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And the wise men always said that one makes a fire cautery also in the middle of the ulcer.
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and I always think it does not seem good, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen before.
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and a more direct thing is that he be cauterized around it, with the fire cautery which is called "circol", as we have said in many other cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of a swelling which cannot perish (die)
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has a disease which is called "adubelati", and it takes long to die or because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say very old) and he has pus in his blood, or because of the time.
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you will see them hasten to die:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then have him cauterized with many small cauteries piercing in.
aprés le laisse ensi.	after that, leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery until its form is like this: (note: there seems to be a blank line or omission in the original text at this point)
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand into the midst of that disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced the core, and be such cauters that the patient feels them all over in such a way that the course of the pus is elevated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards cure him until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure by fire with iron (presumably referring to a surgical procedure using cautery)
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a rotting of the member, for it rots the members as much as fire does dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	if you see this illness in a place where it can suffer cauterization with fire together, then heat the cauteries small and large, according to what is needed for the place where the illness is.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	after that, cauterize him from all sides until you extract all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything which is corrupted be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for 3 days, and apply oil to the places that have been cauterized so that they may boil, until all the burns from fire are gone, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the ointment cure, a scab forms.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	and if after three days you see that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good;
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if not, then reapply the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted places.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this concoction has been cured sometimes with medicinal water instead of fire cauterization.
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but still fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of ague by medicine in its divisions:
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the splinters that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often times it happens that on the feet outside a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large foul growth that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is in two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say fire cauterization, and hot water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery is that you heat the cautery as hot as an oven's iron, and it should be made of good iron to its measure so that it can penetrate a nail from all sides, and have fine edges.
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	then put it all hot on the boil, and turn your hand completely around the boil until it comes to a boil of the boil.
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and let it so for three days until it begins to shed pus.
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then make a poultice of bitter wild mulberries cooked with oil, and let the poultice be on all night, and the boil will fall out and will be pulled out from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place with ointment by applying grease so long as it is sound.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted through the rear part of the body, and often occur in hands and feet, then it is necessary that you bring a cauterization with hot water.
et est en teil maniere:	and it is in this same manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	take a spool of iron or lead, or a nail of copper, and put it on the thorn and the blister, that is to say for removing warts.
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and put the spool on so that it burns all around, then put in a pot of hot water and keep your hand well and press your hand turning so that the edge of the spool comes to the root of the thorn and the hot water can reach deep to the root.
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and let the patient suffer a little the scalding of hot water for an hour;
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then leave him so and it will deracinate itself entirely from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do the same with another, until you have extracted all those that are in the body, then treat them of unguents which cause corruption.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When some person is shivering from cold or from quartan fever or another disease, then you must make for them four cauteries or five on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra.
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one cautery on the foot, and one on the belly over the olive-shaped [cauterization] site.
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	it will leave him trembling, and he will hasten to recover from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	The cure for boils or pustules (puans in Old French). Here is a continuation of the text:
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Some times appear on the outside of the body blisters, or suppurating boils, which come from thick corrupted substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	when it is necessary at first when they appear one must make a cautery over each head of the pustule.
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a fine cautery from a twig of myrtle, the tip of which is taken by fire, or from the root of Aristolochia longa, or a lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And every time one cauterizes them at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow outward any more, but the superfluities from which they come are broken up, and they are healed.
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	But it needs to be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	There are often great losses of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the forefront, or from the incision of the abscess, or from the cauterization of the member, and similar things.
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is a very grievous thing to stop it.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And in any case when it happens to someone, if you hasten to place your two fingers over the wound of the vein, and hold them tight until the blood is stilled beneath your fingers, and no more flows from it.
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then place in the fire the olive oil cauterizers small and large until they are all red.
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take one, either large or small according to the wound and place it on the place where the artery runs, and put the cauterizer on that vein which you hold with your fingers, and hold the cauterizer so long as the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts forth when you lift your finger off the vein, and the cautery is spent, then take another one quickly from among those that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not stop doing these things one after the other until the blood is stopped.
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	and be careful that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that some other evil does not come upon the patient.
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	and know that when blood flows out of the artery, you cannot well stop it yourself, even if the artery is large, unless through one of the four ways we have said.
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cautery, or by extracting it when it is not tied up, or by a strong thread to tie it, or by applying medicines which have power to stop blood.
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and it should be tied and held securely tightly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will remind them of the danger of tightly tying a ligature or putting hot things on it, or similar things, if they do not know what they are doing.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to anyone and he has no physician or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on top of the wound as we have said, and press well until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein.
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and do not move it; but moisten with cold water often as is very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and clotted.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and make inquiry beforehand of those things that he needs for cauterizations and medications.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on surgical remedies.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have already told you in the first chapter of all diseases for which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicines, and the occasions and causes and instruments and forms of cauterizations.
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have placed this chapter from the head to the feet, and I will go through this chapter by the same way in order that what is found to be easier to remember.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and because of that it is necessary to be more careful.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	Where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	Those who have had such a disease that they die easily because of the strangeness they find in their sickness, and the severity of their malady.
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And from this one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And there is someone who gives you his opinion and says:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am grown";
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the disease is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It does not seem right to you that you should consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put greater care in your honor than in your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely towards those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can take and gain.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your patients so that their salvation may be converted;
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to breathe with the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen. (This is a final blessing, typical in medieval texts.)
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter in sections, as I was explaining by chapters, according to what is written before the chapter on cauterizations, which I explained from beginning to end for you, so that you would find it easier to understand the things of which you will need. (This is a conclusion and final statement, wrapping up the explanation of the chapter.)
dou chief plein d’aigue	A vessel full of water. (This appears to be a simple phrase or description, possibly referring back to some earlier context in the text where the use of a vessel was mentioned.)
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this illness often occurs in children at birth, and when the cord tightens too strongly on the head of the child;
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and sometimes it comes from a reason unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this illness occur outside of children, and in all the cases that I have seen, death hastened.
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and for this reason it seems to me that it is worth writing the work about these treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose head was filled with water, and the head swelled each day so that it could no longer be supported;
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the swelling became so great that it was dead, and this swelling is assembled under the bone on top of the scull, between the skull and the bone.
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	And the works are thus if moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you cut in through the head a wide incision.
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and it should also be as long as two ells, so that the moisture flows out;
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and observe its shape of the spatula.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the corners of the head open on each part, and the point jumps high when you press it with your hand from within, and this does not return to its place;
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	so you must cut in through the head three incisions according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision extract all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	Then bind up the incisions with cloth and powder, and put wine and oil into them, and leave it thus until the fifth day.
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then unbind it, and treat the wound with tentatives and with ointments, and let the head be bound up similarly, and give food to the patient dry meat of either moisture so that the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another method of incision is to look where the size of the abscess opens up, and the meeting point of the bone.
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for sometimes it is before [the incision].
aucune fois derrier;	sometimes behind.
aucune fois en destre;	sometimes to the right.
et aucune fois en senestre.	and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Then cut there where the abscess opens up, and the filling of the bone, and do according to what you are able.
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and beware that you do not cut the artery.
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and flowing flood of blood, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	It seems like we've reached the end of this medieval medical text! "De reume" is likely a phrase to conclude the passage, possibly meaning "of swellings" or "on the topic of swellings". If you have any more texts to transcribe or questions about these passages, feel free to ask!
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease that is called "catarre" (likely referring to an abscess or tumor in the groin or armpit) and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last cure is to cauterize with what will close the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	It is necessary then, when you cannot cover them up, that the patient holds his head back.
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	afterwards rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then pull the patient's neck all into the cloth.
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look where the vein runs, and the places of one and both are near the ears, and they should be closed.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then mark the places with ink, then bind one and both with a spatula point of 2 parts long until the vein shows up just to the bone, and that should be done from the top down.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see fit, insert the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting also as two blades through the middle.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood sprays upward continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not open with a needle, then you must measure the length of space of 3 fingers, then mark with ink and proceed up to the bone.
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and that which is to be let out with blood should be 6 fingers, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	then look at the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	if it remains above the bone like a splinter, if pus does not come out of the boils, then close the wound and bind it, and apply ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient headache comes, and sharp catarrh, by reason of the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and old severe fever and similar things, and all manner of medical treatments help him not, then we cut out the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient makes the hairs on their temples grow back and listens to the artery which opens in the temple, for it beats well through its pulsing, and is quickly revealed except in some men who are too cold.
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is revealed, then the patient tightens their neck with some cloth bandages, and rubs the place with a rough cloth, and raises the place with hot water until the artery appears distinctly.
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	then take the spatula whose form is this:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then peel off the thin skin until you come to the artery, then draw it upwards with forceps, and separate it well from the webs that are under each part.
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	and if the artery is fine, then turn it to the point of the needle, and cut off that part according to the quantity of its two extremities.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cauterized, then the blood will not all ooze out.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And drain off the blood from the sixth degree to the third.
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	and if the artery is large, you must tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk, so that no inflammation comes before the wound heals and little by little the blood stops.
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	then tie off the excess that is between the two threads at the same time, and then, if you see fit, apply the fire cautery with the cautery knife up to the bone until the flesh is tied.
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and that is the most necessary work, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For cauterization is help to finish the moisture:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	so it is of even greater aid in the moisters.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and puts on well-made stitches.
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are released, one must be careful of dry medications that cause scabbing, and of tents, until they are healed.
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if blood spurts out from the artery as much as you work on it, then hasten to cauterize with fire, or you take the place of vinegar and hold it in your hand so that the blood is stopped.
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you do not have this present, then put on the place your cloth until the blood is congealed, and raise the place with cold water so that the blood ceases, and hold it as it becomes necessary.
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and what is moist and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize again with this cutting cautery on two parts, but the blades be well thick to hold their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the instruments are too thin, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And it must have between the two knives a piece of cloth, and then when you have sealed both places, and thou dost take the hot iron on top so that it comes just up to the bone, and cut the vein in two parts.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and they shall be pulled apart between the two bones because it is not healed from this fire cautery at all;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and that is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	It seems you've started a new sentence.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears from the eyes are flowing out of the veins that are above the root of the forehead and it does not benefit from the cure of medicine that is done to it, and you see the face of the patient become red, and feels in the front a movement as if of shivering;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and thus if they are warm and moist so that the hairs on the eyelids fall out, and the eyelids themselves are scalded and singed by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary for this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they used to call it the "cure of striking", and you make on the patient who has this illness three incisions or cuts on the forehead equally spaced according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and it should be one of the clefts like the two that are entirely in the forehead while swallowing, and the other two above the kidneys, and beware of the incision of the arteries which are on both sides above the kidneys;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and be each wound the quantity of three knuckles across the joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and moisten it with linen so that the blood may be absorbed, then attach the spatula at two parts of which this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision that is down from the temple to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape all the membrane that is between the two clefts to the full surface which is on the bone, then make another part of the first incision up to the other second, and then draw out with this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument in the first cut, which is called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side not sharp, this is its shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cut side of the scissor towards the inflamed flesh; and the smooth side towards the bone; and press down until it comes to the middle crack.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And close all the blood vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous just up to where the skin appears; and then proceed on the middle cut just up to the other side.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then extract blood evenly, and express the place for the drawn blood.
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put a cloth of old linen in each cut, and place moist cloths on wine and oil and vinegar, and keep so that abscesses do not come to it.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day release the ligature, and administer great application of aloe juice, then the cure with balsam unguent with rose oil, and other treatments by which one heals wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The bond of their bones.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When there comes to anyone accustomed cataract, and you see the eyes tight and small, and weakening the sight, and the eyelids burnt.
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair is shedding, and the head feels intense pain, and the patient coughs;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then you know by these accidents that such materials and the cathartic come out through many veins, and the mother remedy is what it is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient to raise their forehead, then make a great incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one two fingers deep.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the left side of the forehead to the right side, and let the incision be up to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and remove your hand from the nerves at the temples that move towards the mouth;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, let all the blood issue onto an absorbent sponge, and then clean between the two lips of the incision with old cotton and linen rags;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then apply damp cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, and be careful of hot abscesses;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow on it, then treat it with drying things that cause flesh to form.
En teil maniere:	In such a manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of calamine, and make an ointment.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it to these wounds in order to draw out all the pus.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the stoppage of the ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that comes out of the ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or stones, or worms, or pieces of iron ore, or similar thing like iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as yaws, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing thing, like water and ashes, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it festers in the ear, or pierces, or is in another way that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, it will start to drip a drop of purple oil or oil of saponaria, then administer an extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and the patient will sweat with condensation, and plug the nostrils when the sweating comes, and put cloth or wool around the ear.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and there should be an ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Death often comes from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, he should be given an extraction with fine forceps of which this is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it comes out with forceps, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, he should be given an extraction with a fine thread of small stitch.
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not come out with this, make a chain of lead and insert the head of the chain or ear plug into the ear canal tightly, and stop up what is around the chain with soft wax so that blood cannot enter with the chain.
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then pull it out firmly, because death often comes if we have said.
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out in this manner, he takes glue of which birds take, and puts the patient to sleep with any instrument that is pointed for this, and puts a piece of cotton around.
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the glue above the stone or whatever it is, and draw back.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if she does not jump away from all of these things that we have said, then hasten to pierce the ear as soon as an abscess comes into it and a spasm.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of piercing it is that you first make the patient drink something to clean out the cephalic vein, and draw out blood according to its strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty place or joint.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and make the incision as wide as a moon, until you come to the stone, then extract it according to your power, and suck hastily at your mouth.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is cleansed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if there are seeds inside and they swell, administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, then administer a hot poultice made of fine linen according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that abscess.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do that when you think the seed is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it with fine tweezers and a syringe, just as we have said, so that the extraction is clear.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In hot water then that which is in the ear must be used by the patient to stertor with condiments first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it be done on that very same ear itself where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps further because of this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if not, then take many small stones according to the length of your finger, soft and light, and heat them up in a small pot over the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put one or two small stones into the patient's ear, and press on it with his fingers from the other side, and strike with another stone against the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop doing this with stones from stone to stone until the water comes out completely, and thus it leaps completely.
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see this, then take the twig, and insert one end into the ear, and the other end into fire until the thinnest part of the twig is burned.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then do to another part with other twigs as long as the water comes out completely, just as we said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of an animal, if it is small in size, such as a flea and similar things, treat them just as we have said in the division.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of great size that one can feel it, then use the extraction of forceps;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the lighter thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you do the cure as we have said in the division and in treating with distillations, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you look at the ear to the sun:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there are needles nearby, take sharp tweezers; if they do not appear, take the instrument whose shape is this:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it must be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And put the most subtle point into the ear according to the amount of pain from the patient, then suck firmly at the end of the cane;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, plug around the cane with cotton as I said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not come out as we have said, administer distillations which the ancients have tried in the expulsion of worms, and you will find how to treat with distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, whose shape is this as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And let it be of silver or lead plates underneath at the small openings, and above for distilling.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press down inside the distillation with the well-made lead instrument, and if you see it taking hold, take the scraper and envelop it around the tip conveniently with cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then you pour your oil or juice, and all that you see of your medicaments into the jug, and the jug should be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put it into the scraper with all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the smell reaches the patient inside, and let the distilled potion be heated in a pot over the fire so that it is distilled into the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and take care that she is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the stoppage of the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have some perforation in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men through a stoppage of a wound, or from a boil inside the ear, and these stoppages come sometimes deep into the ear, so that one cannot see them;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and often the pus comes out of the perforation, and the sight is well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which comes deep in, and cannot be seen, is a grievous purging in many dispositions, and that which one can see, it behooves you to put the patient's ear into the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the whitening appear, if it has all this spuminess of which this is the shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And be smooth and flat in front and behind, so that it does not hurt the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the swelling is from fat or flesh of the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers and gently scrape it away so that all the fat is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the abscess is open in the ear, then take a fine, light rasor and heat it up slightly over the fire, then put it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the swelling from which the patient feels great grief to the ear, puncture lightly, and be careful not to damage the nerve of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put into the ear a bandage according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a bandage and moisten it in red water, and powder on vitriol powder.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swelling, it is necessary that you remove the bandage and put on another moistened bandage in cerote made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone.

Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the bleeding does not stop, then plunge a sponge and wring it out in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the bleeding which are among the treatments of distillations.
de la char des papieres	I think you meant to say "de la chair des papieras"!
