et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is below;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, if you raise the head with a hot iron or iron rod, or with a cold iron, then place under the tongue a linen pad;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and tie the patient's wound each night, so that the swelling may not subside.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if there is a discharge of pus comes, then apply verdigrease or vitriol plaster on the wound;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the blood flows too much, then cauterize with the slow-fire cautery, which is good for this;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then the patient will be cured of another disease as long as they are healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see the fistula is green or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, because it is a carbuncle;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining towards the bladder and there is moisture, then pour vinegar on it, and make a small poultice with subtle spatium and deliver it from one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the blood flows to your work, then place vinegar-soaked broth on it until it is stopped, then return to your work as long as you drain all fluid;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the swelling of boil and scab, and heal from other diseases as long as he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes a swelling comes inside the throat called "godath", and they are properly called the "amandres", and when you cure them, as we have said in the section, and they are not healed, be careful:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If this is a stubborn abscess of small sense and bloody color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it's red and the root is large, don't touch it with iron, also because of the discharge of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave it alone until it dies, and then you will cut it out, or it would burst on its own;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it's of white color redounding, and the root is subtle, get ready the instrument to cut, but first see if the abscess has cooled down and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and your hand be sure, and the patient open their mouth and take the instrument between their hands, and press the tongue under it all the way to get the shape;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it should be of subtle silver or lead also like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue on this instrument and see the abscess, take the lancet and stick it into the almond, and make a cut up to the surface as far as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and remove any thing that clings with it, then put back the cover on the instrument, of which this is the shape, as if it were a forceps;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and whatever the head is curved, and one side to the other, and are very sharp, and it is made of iron or from a type of steel;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument available, then scrape off with pincers, which is its shape.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And be slotted on one side, and on the other flat.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have covered one of the almonds, if you cover the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and with vinegar, and with ashes, and as the bleeding ceases, gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the blood is stopped;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then the cure must remain until they are healed.
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And at times other abscesses form in the throat besides the two almonds, so you treat them as you would the two almonds that are swollen.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had formed inside her throat, namely the abscess of small sinew.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had well-nigh closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage which was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that I had put in two drains through the two openings of its birth.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened then at once, and inserted an onion into one of the abscesses, then let it drain out, and drew out a large portion of pus.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I reapplied another part to the other opening of the abscess, and moistened the mouth and pressed the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After having filed a needle into these abscesses, and inserted a part of it, and only came out from it a little piece of blood.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the female's throat was cut open, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut into that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess was constantly swelling and filling up the place that I had emptied, so that it became very large again.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I sewed it up and cauterized inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	thus it stayed without growing.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left those parts and God alone knows what became of them after me.
de l’uve	of the urine
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When pus comes down to the eye, and it is inflamed and is long, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is under a thick and rounded [growth], then it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the swelling has subsided, and she is delicate, then it is necessary that you lance it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and the one that is rounded together and not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and she is sanguine or of a bluish or black colour, then you must cut the incision off.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you seat the patient in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention here before.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the probe into the uve, and remove it below, and lance it with the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cut off anything beyond the natural boundary of excess.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut more than this, it will harm the voice and the speech.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, make use of what we have said about the incision of the two almonds, and heal it until it is sound.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about covering, then you must use an instrument at the cautery for the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is hot hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is necessary that the patient puts his head in your hand and then presses the tongue onto the instrument that we have said about in the chapter on cautery, with live sharp charcoal, so that it is not too thick nor too thin.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and fill the end of this instrument, for which there is this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And hold the head with a handful of hair or have someone put the medicine on it, like the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument so that all the medicine is above the eye.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should be placed on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth with the medicine inside, so it does not descend to the throat and the wound;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then take your hand to all the medicine and press it on the eye, for a quantity of half an hour, until you see it darkened and the irritation from the medicine is calmed;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see [the eye], take cotton and wrap it on any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and stick the instrument with all the cotton on the eyelid above, until the cotton dries on the eye;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and apply after 4 days or 5.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to repeat the cauterization with the medicine, then repeat it, and after the cauterization apply a poultice around the eye of cotton wrapped in butter, and cleanse that which is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be risen with cold water, and be cured of gargling until they are sound.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is safer than incision, or the fire cauterization;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calaminth and yarrow and origanum and rue and camomile and avocado and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in a cauldron, and put it over heat, and make it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the cauldron be well glazed with strong earth, and on top of the cauldron have the smoking instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it be of silver or of brass, and the one end be inserted in the mouth of the patient so that the steam rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is numbed.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	afterwards it often recurs, until the eye dries, and be careful that you do not do this at the beginning of the warm rising of the abscess, for many things happen then;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and not make any incision except on the abscess, hot.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a cord and put an egg-soaked cloth in the mouth of the patient so that it may not be too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the egg-soaked cloth does not let the vapour trouble the mouth and this is a good cure together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it has been tried on the throat with an os or the spine of a fish, or anything.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so you must try with what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see how it moves the thing.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not appear to you and is returned in the throat, you must make the patient vomit as soon as the meat is cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	by chance if the thing has been forced out through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of bread dough, or a root of lettuce, or a hard crumb of bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and they tie a thread to the sponge and then have them swallow it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to its place, if it gets stuck, then pull on the thread;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out as we have said, take a plug-in instrument according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can enter more lightly into the throat, and have its head raised upwards;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis so that the whole thing does not come loose, nor push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and make sure the patient puts the instrument in, because it is true that the thing has been pushed out;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the bowstring is let down, or it is pulled out to its full length equally with all the instrument, as far as it goes.
de la sansue de la gorge	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! La première partie du texte semblait décrire une technique de traitement médical pour une affaissement ou un blocage à l'échelle des poumons, et maintenant il semble que le sujet soit la "sansue" (ou plutôt, la sève) de la gorge. Je n'ai pas d'informations claires sur ce que pourrait être cette "sansue", mais je suppose qu'il s'agit d'un terme médical anachronique qui désignait une sorte de liquide ou de flux issu de la gorge.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No blood-letting is medicinally effective, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when it is not beneficial, then look in the throat of the patient to the sun, and then press his tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the pus, then strip it away with a small hook or with fine pincers that are worth for such things.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this doesn't work, then take a horsehair cord and insert it into the throat of the patient, then insert the tip of the hot iron into the cord and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if fever grips the patient every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take full view of cold water, and work the mouth open, and spit it out in his sense unglutinated, and move his hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the blood smells the water, he spits.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not spit as we have said, then subfumigate the patient with asafoetida, at the instrument that I have said in the fumigation of the eye;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will certainly dislodge.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are burning coals, and it be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in this perforation be the handle of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then you throw the fumigation and the patient puts the head of the reed in his mouth and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out but comes just to the nose.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and now the sweat will come forth, and if it doesn't come then you recommence the fumigation many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers thirst and drinks bitter things and herbs and not at all water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it will be necessary for him to go forth through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats bloodletting is such that, when it can be seen, it resembles curved pincers to allow entry into the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it has a resemblance to a bee's stinger and has a roughness of lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go.
et vez ci la forme:	and behold the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Most types of abscess are, according to what the memories come here after from one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two manners by which one is its very likeness, and because of the moisture it contains.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for places where they are within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscess of the head is other than that of the fundament, and the abscess of the joints in the flesh is other than that which comes into joints, and each should have its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if an abscess should not be pierced, as long as the body is soft according to its completion.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and there are such abscesses as it is necessary to pierce when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, such as those that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one lets them be until they are rotten around them, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint become corrupted, by which it is a cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	When the swelling is next to the main member, and if you delay the puncturing until it has died, then it will harm the main member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or it is near the foundation, if one pierces it as soon as it has died;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not necessary that you puncture an abscess which has become hard with completed digestion, because the one that is near the foundation will burst inward and becomes enlarged and a fistula develops;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the puncturing of the abscess which has died according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the diminishment of pain and redness, and the subsiding and quieting of the top of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And it is necessary that you make the puncture sit down to the place where the abscess depends most, and where it opens out.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And the puncture should be long in the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no suppuration.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who have swollen, by displacement of that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the fatty area, it is necessary that you leave the incision so long as it becomes confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you puncture before that, the body will be long with venom in it, and full of pus and filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance they become hardened and the lips of them become thickened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that are pierced in accordance with the length of the body, according to as the member needs it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must bring them to small abscesses, small ulcers.
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in great abscesses, great ulcers, and many splits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if it has such abscesses where you must cut out the core, and sew up.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it is old like a rug, and has become worn out, then you must do the same thing that one does with babies:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if they are like those split into three corners, and if they are like the leaf of the myrtle, as abscesses of the gnat;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if they are like those where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar shapes.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, such as soft superficial abscesses, you must thoroughly pierce them;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and has gathered great pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all of the pus at that time, but draw out a part;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess up to the next day, then draw out nothing from it again.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this by many times of good will, until the swelling goes away.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	even if the patient is weak in virtue, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old men who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pulse beats sometimes with the issue of pus, that by chance the patient dies, and you are not aware.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound drains out, and see if the wound of the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it's a clean incision, try to bind with linen or old cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it's great abscesses, and there is much pus, then you must push in each one a tent so that they come together.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have wrapped it around, then you must fill it with old cotton or a wad of linen cloth without moisture, and tie it until the third day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the bone, and the wound ointment until they are healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs at your work, then administer hot and cold water easily, and moisten the cloth, and place it on the site of the bleeding several times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the purging of blood continues, then give governance and care, and the powders that I have said to be used in the hands as I have written in this book, and if it is the time of summer, and the place or abscess is very moist, so it seems that you should put on tents and wet cloths dipped in wine and hot oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in the heat, and the place is fatty, so it seems that you should put on wet cloths in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then cut open the abscess and drain it and heal it, if it seems necessary, until they are healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is what one needs to know universally in treatments of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	I have told you how to proceed before the treatments of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	swellings
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where tumors come from the head, they are small abscesses, and in manner like spider webs, just as the nesting of a hen, and there are many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are fatty ones and such that also have moisture as well as pus.
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there is such an one that is hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt whether the artery does or does not lie within.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the abscess are that you try all instruments which are called "entromissor", from which the form comes later, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then let it be opened on top of a long (thing).
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture has been emptied, if it should be scraped clean without leaving any skin that contains that moisture behind, for it comes back again when you leave anything.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then plunge cotton in Egyptian balm, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, then in water and vinegar, and apply the dressing to the wound, and leave it until another day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and those who have remained overnight will run.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then start again with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third day, until you know well that it does not remain overnight.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound with ointment as is proper, until they are sound.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds no fat, cut it out according to this shape, long.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and you throw away the stitches, and scrape off from all sides, and put all your care to draw out pus from the place where it is.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery does you harm, do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do with the abscess if it is hard and tough, and of cutting and of healing as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on top of the abscess that is hard and moist, if it is lighter, because they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if to some of these abscesses or in the head or there is no moisture, and among those abscesses that I have cut out or in the head of an old woman.
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess just like a hard, rough and white stone, and could not break it.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if we had cut into any of them, we would have made as good a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	Other abscesses coming from the head, such as those that come to the head of children and to the roots of ears, the opening should always be at most dependent on its place, so that the pus can come out.
et les cure si com il covient.	and they are treated as it is necessary.
des scrophules	Of swellings.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come to other parts of the body, and are foul-smelling, and are intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its coat, such as the boil and abscess on the head, such as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the likenesses of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some boils that contain moisture, and there are some malignant ones that do not want to obey treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one then you see with good disposition to touch, and it is similar in color to the body, and quiet from all parts and is not inflamed at the neck of the collarbone or at the artery or the channel, and it is not deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	so it is necessary that you lance it above, and scrape off each part, and let the two lips of the cure be at the incision, if you need them, such as we have said in abscesses of the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and draw it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and do not make a deep incision, lest your hands escape, and see too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it does not allow you to work, then put vinegar, or some powder that stops blood, in the wound, and hold the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it so until the abscess is calmed, and the wound softens, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work, until you have completed it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then look to see if there remain any small swellings, if so cut and scrape them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is in the root of the swelling a large vein, it does not seem good that you cut that swelling at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang down without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the wound of old cotton dipped in Egyptian oil, then the treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cover the whole scrofula with ointment, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then there is no remainder of excess because of the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofula who hold surplus, pierce there where it emits pus.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce in the same way as that said above, depending, then administer tents with oil and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, then apply the ointment anointing flesh, until they are healed.
de squinance	Squince.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw in our land anyone who did it, and that is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	To those who have swallowed, it is necessary that the cut in the throat called "epiglotte" be closed;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	We do not make aid through this, because all the veins and the body of the patient are at those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in two armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pulse, it is necessary to cut out the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four a small incision through the middle, between the two circles or according to the size of the incision from above, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those places are so suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis that there is no flesh and the vessels are long from being cut.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is timid, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to its full length, then cut the cartilage until it comes to the chin.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the surface, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the tendons of the vein which jumps out from its place that is broken, and by the failure of the ligaments;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed by which we doubt strangulation, gather together the two lips of the wound from the skin and sew them whole without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medications that cause pus to form, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albusimus (a medieval Latin expression meaning "we have sufficiently explained") says that one should not do this just so far as the throat is completely stopped and the patient is judged to be dying, and the wound is giving out pus.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut on the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open as long as the malice of the disease had passed, and it passes in three days or four; and then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat, until it was cured.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young woman take a dagger, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the veins of the privy member.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had come out of it, and I saw well that she had not cut too deep nor gone far into the throat, and the veins were coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I rushed there, and sewed the wound, and cured her so that she was completely healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing happened to the young woman other than that she turned red in the throat, and returned after being back to her usual state.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that when making an incision into the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess of a blackish color, and it occurs very often in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	and it occurs in two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	Congenital conditions, and accidents;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural one has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And accidents are two ways of which one is similar to a boil, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it does not seem right to work with hot irons that in someone who is small, and test and search the whole inner part;
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it in the same way as a boil, and cannot be opened by any means, cut it out, just as one cuts out boils, and treat the whole head if there is no other;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well all around, and cure it as is necessary, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of the nodules.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of boils, whose similarities I will say all;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary for me to say all the difference that is between now and the past.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that past is heat and fever holding, as long as the ebullition has passed, and the putrefaction is accomplished.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then rest from the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the now there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contain's a suppurative abscess, which is his own sack and is according to the colour of the body, and begins also like a blister, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two appearances, either thick or moist, and much in colour are such as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to cure the nodule, that you probe and examine it first with all the instrument called "entromissoire", according to what its form will be, whether it is a head or a pouch which comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of incising abscesses in the body is that you take or find the most moist place within the abscess, and turn your two-pointed tool back and forth, as much as you know that the instrument has pierced to the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then remove the entromissoire and take care that it does not fall.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moist swelling occurs before cutting, whatever its colour may be, do it as I said about other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the entromissoire there comes moist swelling, know that it is fatty, then do it in cross shape, and take with forceps, and scrape lightly from each part and send to the cot where you will pull it out sound with the needle.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out sound, then pull it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will come back many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a small part remains and the blood grieves you, then smear the wound with some corrosive powders sharp, hold the wound tight, put hot soothing things on the warm abscess, and treat it with other cures until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is great, let him cut off two lips of the wound, and cure them with those who are wounded flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein pulsating is contrary or another such as you hasten and apply the location of vinegar to it, and let him leave it for two days or three, until the wound purifies, and rest the ebullition of blood.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cover those which is remaining from the night.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of enclosed instruments, and they are of three manners:
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and among them there are three square ones which are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and among them there are of three manners:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	great, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like the needles for stitching ulcers, and are of yellow gold, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are worth as much as those; and they are more proven to turn black in order to surround the swellings of fistula.
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of needles are of many similarities, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are needles with two points of three kinds as well.
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and there are needles with three points, and they are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and there are needles with two points, and needles with one point alone, and they are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these instruments are sharp, and there are such that do not cut deeply from one side, by means of which we scrape off the flesh, so that neither the vein nor the nerve is cut.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and from these probes are made the linen wraps in hands, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use them at all except in a firm place, such as legs, and arms, and shoulders, and in the elbows, and in similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling a scraper for fingers, according to this shape, with which one stops the blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes in the place where there are cuts of veins and arteries, and sometimes it comes out according to this large shape.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Some times swellings appear on the breasts of certain men when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem to be women's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, should draw according to this form from the line .b. up to .g..
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then peel off the fat and fill the wound with medicinal ointment containing glue, then sew together the two lips of the wound at the edge, and let it heal until it is whole.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast droops down and is swollen like in women, then cut it into two pouches upwards, by two similar incisions.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	in order that the one be held to the other at the end of the one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from the line .b. up to the line .g..
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then skin the leather which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply to it what we have said of sutures and powders, and what is necessary for the treatment, until they are healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if they are not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the bleeding, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with damp cotton in corrosive oil;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it so long as it dissolves the remaining and fat, then treat it until they are healed.
des apostemes des asselles	the nodules of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These nodules that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofulas or carbuncles, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who are moist-affected should be bandaged according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g..
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the nodule has been emptied, then fill the wound with fresh cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat it with soothing oil as needed until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the nodule is of a similar nature to carbuncles, then treat it as we said for incisions of carbuncles, and if the wound fills with pus again, then apply cauterization as we said before.
de la routure de l’artere	the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut and the skin above is sewn up, then there are often abscesses, and it also happens that the vein becomes inflamed and forms an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows thus when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your hands, then feel its stiffness;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and if it's for the vein, it is reason to fear something appearing outside.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolishness to cover this abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and the groin and the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Then you should shun the iron treatment, and also that which is on the head, and in him who is inflamed with an artery, do it above the skin of the long flesh.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work on the limb by the incisions, and carefully separate the artery from the tendons, until it is uncovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then place under the one a needle, and have it pierce to the other side, and bind the artery with a doubled thread in two places, according as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then mark the spot where it lies between the two strings of a pulley so that the blood which is in it comes out and the abscess is loosened.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then bring the bandage to the incision, as far as the stitches sink in.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then apply that ointment which is suitable for it until they are healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is because of the swelling of the vein, then it is necessary that you draw with your hand what comes out from the abscess all over the skin, and then insert the needle under the spot which you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there will be two threads, so that you pull them from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I told you, or tie with a thread one of its two parts to both ends.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the thread will not come out, then insert another needle in place of all the thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess so that the superfluities come out, then cut the excess of flesh and leave what is joined.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a moist cloth in wine and oil, then administer to him the cures of tents and unguents until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	the nodules of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also like nodules that come to the artery and the vein, nodules also come to the nerves when they are irritated or due to excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this occurs more often in the joints and in the elbows and in all places where there are articulations, and it is a grievous abscess, and its colour seems like the colour of the body, and it is in many dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one holds it firmly, then the patient feels pain, and it is not in the very depth of the body, but under the flesh.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and is able to move freely from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor up or down, and he who is in joints should by no means cut with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	perhaps there will be constriction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is in the head or on the forehead, should bind with a strap.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, take it with forceps and cut out at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, suspend it with a thread and peel off the skin, then remove the abscess and sew up the wound to the stitch, and let the cure continue until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large, hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes it occurs in the abdomen and not elsewhere than that, and it is a disease which is called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots and a large head.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are small and very large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I have seen in one person who had two or three on the belly that were more like mushrooms than any other thing, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a small root, and were already splitting open, and would constantly drain moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I copied them and found one to weigh eighteen ounces, and the other six and a half pounds, and in the operation of incising them it is that you see whether the patient is moist, and the color of the abscess is white and moist and with a subtle root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if it copes on the shoulder blade wide, and you are present with the cautery by fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For when cutting comes too great a bleeding of blood, and the patient faints, then you hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	And if you see the patient shuddering and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made thread of linen, and tie the arm so as we have said, and leave it for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then hold fast, and cease not to hold the linen thread tight until it ties up the arm, and he feels by his own effort.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are thick, he will be afraid to cut them right through for his belly, but you can well cut the middle part, then cauterize it so that it does not relapse.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then heal the wound, and be careful that you do not cut the nodule which is of rough colour and poor sensation and with milk-like discharge.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an infected nodule, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the pus has been emptied out.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from a cautery wound or an abscess cut open on the abdomen and some of them burst like in other wounds, or from blood that runs out through veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it's by the bursting of the abscess and by the discharge of pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and it is evident from various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is much more varied, and when one presses it with their hands it swells up, and then goes back down, and perhaps it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and due to great exertion.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it's because of moisture, it's a light thing, and you can see well when you press it with your hand, and it does not bind at all.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it's because of blood, then the abscess is apparent through these signs, large and hard, and it has a definite quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it's because of windiness, then it is soft to the touch, and the operations are such that you look to see whether the appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary for you to leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, it behooves you to instruct the patient to strain his bowels, and have him stretched out straight, then sign for a poultice to be wrapped all around the belly.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then command him to lie often between your hands; then go around the joint that you have marked with a suture needle at all the spatula-like edges; then cut off half of the abscess above at all the large incisions.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie him around with a strong thread, or with a cord of strong silk firmly, and the stitches should be well loosened.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then operate on half of the abscess stretched over the thread, and insert your thumb index finger, and probe the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught on the thread, then loosen it, and push the intestine back into the belly from outside.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the fistula, then catch it with the forceps, and excise the redundance.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the vein or artery gets in your way, then go around it gently, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert the two threads, and tie the two needles around what you have done so that you pierce it.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in four places above the needles; and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the place until it suppurates, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is softened and suppurates; then the wound heals from what it needs, and you let the abscess drain as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and draw out the blood or moisture that you find; then dress the place with what it needs, and knit the bone.
dou chancre	It seems like we've reached a section of text that doesn't follow the previous instructions on how to treat an abscess.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division of ulcers how similar they are to a carbuncle, and how one must work with them by medicine, and how one must avoid treating with iron.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and we say that a carbuncle spreads into the marrow, and great caution is needed in its cure; and the ancients said that when ulcers are in places where one can shave them, such as on the breasts, and in the thighs, and in similar places, and they should be completely removed at the beginning.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is old and ancient, you must not approach it, for I have never seen a healthy one;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	never saw anyone recover from it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the works, when it is in place or can be removed as we have said, are that you bleed the patient of black bile once;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make him well if he has manifest fullness, then prepare the patient in good health to do the work;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then cut out your ulcers or cancers, and shave his hair from all parts, and scrape off all his skin with nothing left;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and press the place well with your hand or something, and if there is bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding is stopped;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat them with another treatment until they are healed.
de ydropisie	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have already said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure which is done by medicine, and that which is cured by iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is clear only;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not touch them with iron in these two likenesses:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and hypochondriasis, because it is a mortal thing.
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	so when you medicate this likeness of dropsy which is called "eclites" by medicine, and the cure does not help, then look to see if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness other than dropsy, such as a boil and an ulcer in the stomach and similar things;
