et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman stayed sick for a long time in this way, and soon she had a small lump of pus from the wound.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have forgotten this chapter until now that, when a master finds an unusual thing, he knows how to intervene.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the flesh to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Then comes the form of the purgation, by which one evacuates books;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and to two returns to the two shoulders.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle than the pincers, and are made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the opening of the handle should be two palms wide, and the edge of the trees a little over one and a half palms;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two straps should be two joints of this same handle, which should be closed in one and in the other, a half palm long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two joints are inserted into the mouth of the handle to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, made from ebony wood or boxwood, should be fashioned with a similar appearance that is more delicate and lighter.
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and have two notches on it, just as you see them, a palm in length, and two fingers in width;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you open the instrument all the way, have the woman sit on a bed, her feet together and her legs apart, then insert the two notches together into the vagina, and hold the handle of the instrument under between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand with the entire instrument, just as you have done with the pincers equally, according to the size that you see opening up the mouth of the vagina, until the ball does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all topped and have many similar forms;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the surgeons have prepared them, so is the work more urgent, and higher for men by their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument if you have not prepared it, for its needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it behooves you to command the patient to retain her afterbirth, and then have her sweat with conditius, and bind her hands to her mouth and belly.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she falls from this, well is it.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take a poultice, and make the pertus or coverlet, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the uterus, such as calamintha, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or any of them, should be cooked or steeped in water over the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put a string or coverlet on the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the uterus, and tie it so that the vapors come inside the uterus.
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	Then one must sternutate, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine jumps out hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment and is not cured, instruct the nurse to moisten her right hand in sesame oil or mullein seed paste, and then apply it to the natural place, and tie a bandage.
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she has found it, take hold of it and stretch it bit by bit straight out, so that the ligaments do not tear during extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but it must be moved lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull.
si venra et se desaerdra.	it will come out and become dislocated.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the ligaments is constricted, as we said the treatment for sternutating, and fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it does not come out of all that we have said, be careful not to force it.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	But it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the wound be tied to the vulva of the woman; then fumigate with ointment quadrifarmaceutical.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	If the purgation and resetting happen, and it comes back again.
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	But however, when she purges herself badly, a foul odor comes to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	So it is necessary to do fumigations convenient to those things:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	None of the ancients have tried fumigation with sorrel and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman at retention of flowers and secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is like seeing a chain, and one puts the head of it subtle in its nature, and the joints wide over the fire.
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be over the coals, and the lice so long as they are spoiled, and then start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation (of the uterus)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but rather it is stuffed by subtle siphacs.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so then it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that siphac at its base, and not with a sharp spatula, and secure the ligature so that it does not touch.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on linen soaked in wine and oil, then apply salve until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not set, then put or make a poultice with a string, and let it be on for many days, and remove it when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And this stifling often comes from a sudden wound or an abscess.
si covient coper celui soudement:	so it is necessary to cover that wound:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	if it is cured, as we have said of the cord of a poultice.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula of the fundament (or anus)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from under the fundament are notched and growing like those that come outside the fundament forward, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more.
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	And when that lump is old, if it works, and the moisture gathers in white or subtle swellings, and sometimes these abscesses persist.
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are caused by those who spit out or discharge pus, or vomiting, when the patient makes an evacuation, and it may happen that some purging occurs.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there are abscesses that burst just to the bladder, and just to half of the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach as far as the crotch joint, and as far as the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows a persistent abscess at the fundament, and not non-persistent.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you probe your heel or fundament, and insert a fine needle of silver or iron into the abscess when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twisting, then you insert a thin silver probe or the hair of a horse, as long as you feel the probe or the hair on your toe.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no bloody discharge or wind or pus, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	know that it does not pierce.
si te haste dou curer.	if you hurry to heal.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces down to the bladder or down to the urethra, then the urine comes out and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it has pierced just up to the joint of the thigh, the tendon comes just to its place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the origin of the pain around it, then it is that it has come to a bowing, and it does not worth medicine nor binding by ointment;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these pus-filled abscesses there is no strong cure except toil, and the vanity of foolish healers who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In the one that is not yet pus-filled and is not old, there is hope of recovery by iron, as I have proven, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on their back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and lift his legs up to his thighs, and have his thighs inclined towards his belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put an iron bandage, or a wooden splint if there is deformity, as long as you know where the splint comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it near the fundament, then you should insert your middle finger, and if he then feels the splint has pierced.
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and be discovered where you feel between your thumb and skin or flesh, then know that it is a sinew.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if there is no swelling at all, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is said that some people can heal well, but this is rare.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid given to it, is that you cauterize the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and tie it all hot on the fistula, so long as it comes near the fundament.
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two times or three, until you know that these charred places are cauterized, which are similar to a bird's feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat with moist tents in butter, until the charred places issue forth pus, and then treat with ointment anointing the scar and healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If that, otherwise it cannot be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent goes in and does not pierce just to the doth that is on the fundament, and between your skin and the tent there is a thick covering of charcoal or of syphac, and you see the fistula at this which closes the covering from the heat.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if the pus comes out at the beginning of the fistula, and tie it up straight away in front of the tent, and after cauterize the caustic so long as it comes to the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and it will be given to him, the tent, and he will shed;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then remove those old scabs that look like a bird's feather, and let nothing remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound swells up, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicinal water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cautery gathers two kinds of things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	that is to say, the scorching of those old scabs and the drying up of blood and the withering of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the cure for wet tents in mud or dung brews, until the place discharges pus, and the scabbed flesh peels off into the pus;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wound with ointments that soften dry skin, and are the dried medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it has been restored, then it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes right down to the fundament and is far from the body, then stick your finger into the fundament and inspect it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you sense the tent and there are two layers of web or pus or scab that is about to burst, if there is no fire but only a sign of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	You to it cauterize if you want, or you cut him just to the bottom, or if you can put some tents and cure as we have said first.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too far in depth, lest you cut the covering which holds the foundation, and the evacuations come unwillingly.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then heal it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will heal, or you remove that covering and clean it then, since it has been cut near the foundation, with a tent or another instrument assigned;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cleanse thoroughly the foul flesh which is in the wound as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound and to stay the fistula in the part opposite the foundation:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And there are no more fistulas in this manner:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And is when you pierce the tent in the fistula, and it is near the edge of the foundation to the skin above, take a tented pin at the head according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and insert one twisted thread in two, and insert the tube into all the thread in the fistula as far as it goes to the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread of that pin, thus as you pierce your needle into the foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and pull the head of the thread, and join the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and let it stay for a day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and hold it in place once, until the threads dry and bind together, and congeal.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it to pierce in all ways that you can, as long as it is not too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make a hole that is too deep and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spine-like splint for making a fistula is very much in one part and tapered.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand not, therefore we do not pierce that which should not be pierced, as you see here:
des emorroydes	the curved ones.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Men are according to two manners:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are inside the fundament, as grains of resin, and there are small ones and large ones, and in them there is blood, and there is one or more of them, and they protrude from the fundament and at the top of the fundament.
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that protrude have a mass of moisture, and in them there is a drop of clear water or a drop of blood, and they have the color of flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment of those that are inside the fundament, is that you instruct the patient to strain himself so as to urinate in chamber pots, until the fundament emits out from it, and it becomes clear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hasten, and grab it with forceps, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut into its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the moles cannot be held due to their moisture, then take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camel's hair.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and extract them to your shoulders, then cut, and powder over some hot powders that are in place of fire cauterization;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cauterization, then heal from other treatments until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the fundaments cannot come out, then enema the patient with a biting and sharp purge to wash what is in the fundament, so that it may come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	if the patient feels himself, and if his string are strong from the fundament, then is the cure easy;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you grasp them with your nail or in tongs, and cut, then heal them as we have said, until they are healed, and so that the incision by iron does not occur.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	it is necessary for you to suture the wound in this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread, and insert it into a needle, then draw the thread upwards and make the needle puncture from the other side, and turn both ends of the thread under the needle, so that it is loose.
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and hold the thread tightly, then tie the thread, and draw out the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one for correction of the excess of blood.
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place a moistened linen cloth on the fundament in rose oil or in cerote, and place it on the fundament, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let him be as long as he urinates, and when they have finished, then treat them with ointment and other treatment, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the drying up of the fundament or fundament's opening.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying up of the fundament in the intestine, and by natural constriction, and when the sickness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is necessary that you reset at the tip of a spatula or with your nail the scab above, which does not let it become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal them as soon as possible when it is needed;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be healed, then re-open the wound more strongly than before, as long as it heals somewhat, and is cleaned.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal them as soon as they are healed.
dou fremit	from the flux.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A boil is a small false appearance on the body, and goes quite deep;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and any time it finds its way into the bone, and the flesh feels just like dead flesh, with a sense of numbness, and comes to every part of the body, more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a thread of goose quill, or a strong boar's bristle, and put that thread on top of the boil, until the red circles encircle the boil completely;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand around the whole thread so that it completely encircles the boil, and put it deep in, and squeeze out the boil from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, then do as with a thread of silver or iron according to this shape, and make it subtle below and draw it above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Do not pierce, for movement is to be held at two, and move it tightly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, then cauterize the tremor, as is shown before this chapter on cauterizing.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the clyster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	At any time make a catheter of silver or copper, or melted lead, or linen cloth;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and at any time make these instruments small and large, according to the size to which they are adjusted.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are administered in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large clyster is as follows: above wide, or the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and it has a rupture or the belly is bound closed, as you see, and the navel string is pierced inside;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and it has two holes on one side, and in the other one.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly is sewn with medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and has between each hole one span of space, then put in these holes a strong thread of twisted hemp yarn or cord in an X shape or around, and assemble the belly as if it were a goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong string beforehand, then apply the poultice;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	and let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the poultice with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then put it on lightly;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the attendants will hold it with both hands together until it is completely soaked, then remove the poultice, and lift the patient's legs to the height, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it drip as much as it can;
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps one night straight through, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize him in the disease of purging of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it as many times as necessary until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are on the foundation or abscess, then the poultice will be just as subtle for him as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle blister on which the skin is restrained:
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the division about the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicines, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are through a stone falling, and cutting with a sword and knife or lance or club or arrow or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or those which are made according to the places of the body, such as wounds that strike on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from falling of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn up and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt of hot abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if it is done immediately to stop bleeding from the head itself if blood flows from the wound, and the bleeding occurs on the opposite side of the injured area;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and instruct the patient to abstain from wine and thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to heal, let him reduce his meat and not drink wine or chew on any flesh;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put sourness on the wound, if a blister forms there, cotton soaked in rosed oil alone, or in wine vinegar;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot blister, put on the wound a powder that I will speak of later in this chapter;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the burn has healed it, then put on some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot come together by themselves, then bring them together by stitching, just as I will say about wounds of the belly, in the chapter on stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is open to the bone and is gaping and only holds by a little, then cover it.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then treat the wound with medicine and restore hard flesh in place of skin; and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as cooked heads and bread, also fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a wound with putridity, and it has not reached the bone, then scrape off all the putrid part, and throw away pus; then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without covering it, and it cannot be stopped with medicine, then ligate the artery; and if you find it severed, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is easy.
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and you put in this powder which heals just as soon as the ointment has dried.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	The manner of the powder is this:
pren encens une partie;	take incense a part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	blood of dragon two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	powder the live salve three parts, and powder finely, and apply the wound, and hold it firmly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then tie it well, and let it be without untying, if it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not remove the medicine until she is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes we do this with lime alone, when we don't have incense or dragon's blood, but the inflammation has already made the wound swell.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the ulcer has moved the wound, even to the inside, one should not put this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but place above some digested ointments, or a poultice made of wheat flour mixed with water and honey, until it discharges pus;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the patient is cured with other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a fracture of the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then draw out to fine forceps.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you here after about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is a clean wound, so there is no other cause than to leave it and not put anything restraining in it, for it harms the nerves and makes them recede.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but put on the medicine sweet, such as calamus dissolved in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber dissolved also in sweet water, and other powdered herbs according to this manner, and moist salves.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and tie with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and they are in the head and full of pus, so pierce or lower than that.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, then one must sew it up, and bind it with a bandage, and apply fire to cauterize it;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduit is guarded, by which the flesh goes, then sew up the wound on the jawbone of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it correctly, and let it for some days, then treat it with ointments that are discarded until they are healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then sew it up;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are bone fragments, then extract all that you can, and leave those which you cannot remove, until the wound purifies, dries out, and adheres to its outlet;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on it the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then cure it thus as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the stab wound or cut
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, look if there is gas or wind escaping from the wound of the patient.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep and all the blood has not dried in it yet, do not put powder on it nor bind it right away because the blood will dry inside and return to the heart and kill the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I put attracting ointment on it, and tie it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and make the patient sleep over the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	If there is no spasm, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor stretching out with strain.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good outcomes, then you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal it with stitches and other treatments, until it is sound;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal or close, then you know that there is an abscess.
si la cure si com on doit.	if the treatment is done as we must.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is a cut from sword or knife, and it is superficial, in front or worse, on the back, then treat what shows.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is great, with stitching.
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder, and if it has pierced the bone and broken into splinters, then clean out the wound, and cut out the torn flesh.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not severed, then let the wound rot, then it will ease the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds on other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of a broken or ruptured uterus
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great and middle-sized and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a large wound sometimes the intestines burst forth, or the membranes of the intestines, through which their insertion;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes is worth worse than the small wound that the large one, for this reason one puts more to pins the intestines in, if one does not put them in hot in hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell at once when they feel cold, so they are sewn up more tightly, and for this reason is it better than the middle-sized wound, because one stitches back the intestine to its place rather than the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that intestinal rupture is according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common wounds occur in the abdominal wound, and the wound of other body wounds and two other proper wounds are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and nonetheless they are more proper with the abdominal wound, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine has come out, and a small thing is to be put back, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	soak an sponge or a wet cloth in hot water only, or cook in hot water with cyperus and spike, and apply the intestine so that the swelling is removed.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and at any time made this wine restraining, and it is known that there is sole for deflation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestines with vinegar or ale and boil them badly, for by this is relieved the entrance of pus into some thing.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a poultice with the wound at the instrument of which one cuts the hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is known that cutting, that no one should cut without great necessity there be not;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so cut inside in the hollow and not outwards, and see thus its shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have jumped out, so place them back again according to their natural form in their proper place, if you are able, for this will be useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and it is in the part under the belly, then you must have the patient lie on his back and put his legs higher than his head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, so place the head and pelvis higher than the parts below, and also the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts so place your intention that the hurt part be higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it behooves you to remember what I say about great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	in small wounds apply what you are accustomed to, then take in your hands the minister of poultice which covers the whole rupture with his hand and close the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common method of stitching, and it is that you take one needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave a space from the head of the wound of about an inch, and insert a needle where there is good thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the awl which is inside the skin, as far as you make it pierce from that part, and join the two ends of the awl together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then the strain of a doubled thread around the needle of two parts, then join the two edges of the wound inappropriately, and then leave it for a space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the double thread as you did the first needle, and cease to do this with needles as often as you need them, until all of the wound is strained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and be the needles old, between fine and thick, for the fine needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot well enter;
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they are old;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it does not help to thrust the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, that they cut and open the wound in front of the suturing;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then sew the threads of the needles so they do not irritate the patient while sleeping, and put tents or cloths over the threads of the needles to keep them from moving, and leave them until the wound is sutured;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this manner of stitching with needles is more advisable in small wounds, for it suffices with one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitching is common, and it is that you assemble the two pieces of skin and the two pieces of flesh together with one needle in which there is one strong thread in the middle;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced all four pieces together, then remove the needle at the part where you began, in the manner that one sews cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a thread of the thickness of a small coin between each stitch;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	this stitching is known to men, and I sewed up a wound that a man had on his belly, which was injured by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm long, and it reached as far as two palms into the intestines, and the wound was on the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back to his intestines after he had been 24 hours empty, and the wound was sewn up just in 15 days, and I healed him, and he became whole.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had judged that he was dying, and it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not treat him with oil, for I was in the place where one cannot find it, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and placed honeyed water on it three times a day, and washed the wound until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching.
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and push it from the outside part up to the inside part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the core straight through, then turn the tip of the needle or stitch where you had put the needle in, and make it pierce from the inside part up to the outside part.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as tailors do with furs, and leave it once on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of stitching, which the Gauls call properly, is such that some do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the suture to the other end, in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	thread a needle or head of a thread close by, and make it pierce only that place, and let the two ends of the suture remain.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from outside to inside, up to the inner part, with the two ends of the suture.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from outside to inside, in two other holes of the thread that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the simpler manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	The Gauls call this phrase thus, and some testify to it, that the belly should be sewn with two needles, or thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must insert a needle from one side and the other, in the manner of those who sew gut.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is within the belly, it is more grievous than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as that of the other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, even as the burn has changed it, then sew back the intestine and the belly.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on the powder of burnt charcoal, and if the burn has changed it, then put on any salve that is present, until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and bind the thread, and sew up the sinew and the muscle.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound as the others, until it is whole.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you don't have medicine, put on as soon as it starts to ooze pus, old cloth, and move it twice a day until it is clean.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	for in many cases when wounds are simple, you don't need any other medicine;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will become a communal infection with the main limbs, it is necessary that you anoint light linen in tempered hot oil, or rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if he feels pain or stench in the bowels, and it often happens, cleanse him with a black wine purge made of hydromel, and similarly if the stench comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and probe inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more easily healed than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are hurt, and this is because of the emptiness of their veins that are in them, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the approach of its nature to the nails.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine bursts out of the wound, replace it back inside just as with the intestines, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has turned green or black, you must bind the place that is black so that blood does not come there, for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cover what is between the bandage, and hang the two ends of it down from under the wound all the way to the outside so that the extraction is facilitated when the intestine drops, and the wound bursts open.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, one can sometimes restore it in certain people, because I have seen a man who was wounded in the belly by an arrow.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the belly and it became covered and turned into an ulcer, and from it there came out purulence and windiness.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied a treatment according to what I knew, and I did not stop subtleting until they were healed, and the wounds sutured.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it close, I doubted that the patient had an illness in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experienced ones said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he must be bound in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take a poultice on large stones, then bring the edges of the wound together, and when the poultice has opened its mouth, so put it on the two lips, so that it tightens its mouth on;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then bind the head with it, and it will hold so that he cannot untie it, and then put another poultice after in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and cover the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the head of the dislocation is in the intestine, and it causes no harm to the patient, then one can tie the intestine with a thin thread that is made from the intestine of an animal, in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the head of this intestinal thread that is very clean, and then tie to the end of this fine linen thread twisted, then insert the thread in the needle, and sew up the intestine, and set it right again.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing with thread is nothing other than according to the way of faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the grooved intestines, then there is no remedy nor recovery except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of an ulcer or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is universally called a "fistula"; and indeed when it is filled with pus and flows downward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	A fistula is a hard and white abscess-like thing that forms according to the direction of the node, where one does not feel pain, and it is also hollow like the quill of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And at times in a clear bow [is used], and sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	and sometimes thin, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it's only because of one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the weakness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because it has hard flesh within and on the edges that does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much pus;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the wound is rotten and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the property in that region is slow in digestion and slow in healing, and follows its natural course;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary that I inform you about the treatment for fistula made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in every member of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the bladder, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and thus it can occur in the property of the principal member, and similar lesions.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is no remedy except cutting and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not come all the way to the place that I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you know it well, take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, cut into it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the fistula is twisted, then search for it with a thin probe to plunge in, because the probe bends around its twistiness.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search for it with probes, then purge it through one of the openings, because the moisture runs from one opening to another, and purify.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then seek a puncture to your ability, knowing if there is bone or nerve, and it is sharp in depth, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when pressing with your hand, and where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you will truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut away according to what I have said, and take out the bad formation and the corrupt flesh that are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure until it is healed; and if the fistula is well dug from the right place, it is necessary that you go deep as far as you can; then put wet sponges soaked in medicine poultice on it, and keep them tight to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the remaining excess at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put salves or unguents on fresh clean flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if they are not healed by this, then cauterize them as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then scrape it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or nerve does not strike or hurt a main member, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackening, so remove it as long as the corruption is completely gone, then treat with things on fresh flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if they are not clean, and turn blue like before, know that you have not gone all the way to the bone:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it is uncovered and bleeds as much as you need to go all the way down, and remove all the corruption, then restore it to its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is thus cleansed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	if not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot intervene;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy except to let it go according to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can extract it with pincers, then extract it with the instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, then extract them all, not leaving any;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture hinders you, and there is no error or fear, then cut and clean out the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put on the wound a thing causing corruption and let it be like that until the flesh is corrupted around the bones, and then they will come out more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, as of the leg or thigh, remove only the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then close up the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great part of the corrupted [flesh] and it comes just to the bone's marrow;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	you should cover and close up all just to the corruption, and then heal him until he is sound.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of an abscess which occurred in a man on his leg, so that you may take it as example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man of about thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from an internal cause that came into the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and he was swollen with a large abscess, and had no reason to open it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the physicians, through their foolishness, worked so much above that they opened the abscess, and flowed out a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and there came a lot of pus that all spat forth and moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many physicians put a cure around him for two years, and there was no skill in the art of hands, until I was called to it, and saw his leg and the remedies by which he was being treated, and what flowed through the pus with great force.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitch a tent in one of these holes, and then search all the holes, and find that one comes up against another from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hurried then, and cut into one of the ulcers as far as I could expose a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption had come right up to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I cleaned away what appeared of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except for what I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with medicinal ointments over a long time, and it could not be sutured.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the continued corruption in the bone, and cleaned it, and then extracted it, and bent myself to sew back the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I was not able until I cut around a palm of the bone, and drew it forward to its entire length, then restored it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healed and sutured quickly, and there was no need to begin the treatment again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the evacuation [of blood], it often bled profusely, but was completely cured, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and it was in good condition and had no harm or disadvantage from beginning to end, whether at coming or going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it must be sewn in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take a cord, and bind it to the head of the bone that is open, and command someone to stretch it upwards.
