et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And put another cord of linen that is larger than the first cord, and bind it on the flesh that is over the bone, and stretch the head, so that you draw out the corrupt flesh below, and uncover the flesh above to the place where you see soundness, so that the sound part does not wound the flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And put an iron or a wooden spatula beneath the bone to move and scrape out the corrupt flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to make as sound and as clear as one can see and feel the corruption, and to make sound again another time also.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put an iron beneath, and then make sound from one part to the other the corruption, and be the wound sure of length as long as the corruption is, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and be on the other side of the bone where it contains.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other remedy but to cut.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the wrist of the foot, then that thing is very strong indeed, but nonetheless it is necessary to inquire into that ulceration and how it appears.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways you know, but beware of the vein or the nerve causing opposition.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the saw and the needles to cut these bones are many, according to the place of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and so therefore it is necessary to prepare for every kind of operation his instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument of which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if thou considerest the instrument of which thou hast need according to what it is necessary.
dou feu	and from fire (to sterilize and purify).
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head can dislocate either because of an internal reason or because of an external one;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when thou hast used medicine to cure that corruption and it does not help, then you must cover that member up to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes by this means from death or from the more serious evil of the defect of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire, and after the blackness pus goes forth from the corruption of the member into the member, and takes hold throughout the body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you have haste from a snakebite, and it is because of the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as the scorpion of the sea and viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is in the head of the joint of the hand, then strike it, and do not give him space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, then strike at the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes up to the arm, then strike at the elbow.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no other remedy than the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do thus also when the corruption comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, then strike after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes on the foot, then strike all the foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it occurs in the leg, then cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of cutting or sawing the member is that you tie it above and below, stretch one servant's cord downwards and another servant's cord upwards, and you loosen the skin that lies between the two cords to a width of about an inch, so that the bone shows.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or saw it, and place a strip of linen on either side, so that the saw does not touch the sound bone, and another lesion and swelling will come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if there is bleeding from the wound when you work, then cauterize the area quickly, or place some astringent powders on it.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable cord, and treat it so that it becomes sound;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened at my house in my own village:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he had a burn that seemed like fire, and that burning came first to the skin of his foot so deep that it reached right through the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the burn, he had himself covered with a poultice on the foot and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and after a long time the burn came back to the skin of his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things that are repercussive after the purification of the body, and the burning could not cease;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I had hope of recuperating the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted whether if I had cut off his hand he would have died, for the virtue of man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he lost all hope and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and it healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have this account on record only because of that which is done in another way, if need be.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Often a swelling occurs in the fatty part, and stays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and breaks open, and the pus jumps out, and leaves the place bare, just like when a wine vessel bursts.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin on top is just as delicate as a loose and fine cloth, and they do not run all the way to the bone or to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain", and it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes right to the bone deep inside, then it is called a "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is that you cover him completely with cloth, and just as we do with a delicate cloak;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it should not be opened for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have faith that the skin is opening and the corruption is not in deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it with a poultice.
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	examine if the breast is large and the nipple which comes out of it has a foul odor, then apply an Egyptian ointment made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take assafris, and oil, and litharge, all equally, and put to cook in a clay pot over the fire, so that the medicine is red, and becomes just as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take it according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and cleanse the chest, and hold the pit steady.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for 2 hours, then extract it by pressing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the chest is purified, and the impurity is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and at any time when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes of vine wood, pour water over them, then let it run, and cleanse with it, until you know that the chest is well purified.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot suffer it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then cleanse him with water and honey, or he has a pot of white lead powder.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or cleanse him with honey and mead wine, where the honey has properties to purify and wash, and the wine makes the sweat;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this, and you are confident that the breast is well purified, then cleanse it with a poultice that causes pus to form in it; and take diaphrenetic plasters, and make them with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken the properties or treatment of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the perforation of the breast is small, and the syringe's nozzle cannot enter it, then enlarge it with a point of iron and put on a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too wide, then cover and leave it just at the level or the location of the syringe so that it can enter; and if the perforation that spouts blood is above, put a bandage lower than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowstring is drawn to its fullest extent, do not let it relax.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the chest as far down as you see, then arrange in such a way that the bowstring runs to its lowest point; for when the bowstring is fully drawn, do not let it relax and if you cannot cover the chest as far down as you see, then arrange.
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the bowstring runs lightly downwards, and let nothing of the bowstring relax.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidative medicines to put on the shoulder, and apply them on the linen cloth that covers all the shoulder.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover the area where the chestnut-shaped hole of the shoulder is, making a pocket as much larger than the first one; then apply gentle ointment on the other cloth according to the size of the hole, and put it on the hole of the shoulder to loosen the bowstring, and do not remove the great cloth that will be used later once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And that which is on the pit of the breast, is often cut off to remove the tumor, and you should know whether it flows from the tumor, if it is venom or pus or enough or digestible or indigestible.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this manner and you see what kind of nature flows on the pit of the breast, then know that the breast is already affected, and approach a surgeon.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then tie it in the morning or the third day, and when you untie the wound, if it has changed its dressing, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the milk flows with undigested blood for many days, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come out after a long time, do not lose hope of health, for the patients approach health.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose wounds do not heal promptly with flesh in them, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the undigested pus flows from the breast after many days, then know that the breast has not been affected.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the wound is slow to heal and is foul-smelling, then apply medicated salves that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diachylon ointment, because it contains a great part of vinegar, and this is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diachylon ointment, and make it with rose oil, and add equal parts of old wine in quantity.
puis le confit et en use;	then boil it and apply it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and doing the same thing makes a better thickened honey syrup, when diachylon ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind it, and powder it over the honey as it is on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then anoint with it a linen cloth, and place it over the wound, and at any time administer a cerate of long storax, and roots of lily flower, which is also like flour of aloes and candle grease.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and with simple or compound plasters:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them and make powder, and lay the honey that I said on it, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is long and not healed by this treatment, then know that corruption has gone deep, and made impression in the bone, or hard flesh, or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if it is a cure of the abscess (fistula) as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil or pustule on the finger.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Paronychia is an abscess that forms under the nail of the hand, or foot, or perhaps forms in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it becomes old and no attention is paid to it, then the abscess bursts and flows and discharges pus as long as the nail runs its root, and perhaps it discharges all.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corruption just to the bone, so much that there is stinking pain, and the head of the tooth is wide open, and the colour is bluish.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not profit, then you must cut into it all the way through with a sharp knife, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauteries are a great aid if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to prick, and to wound, then it is necessary that you place the tip of the cautery on the point of the nail that pricks the flesh, and push up high, and gently and lightly press upon that flesh, and put on the rest of the flesh medicines hot and corrosive in order to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then scrape and clean it, for as long as the corrupt bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the joint to be corrupted, then scrape in at the joints as was said before, and then cure it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is festering, and swollen, and he feels great pain, then it is necessary that you clean it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the navel of the scapula at an angle by cutting across, and be careful that the cut does not reach to the flesh which is under the navel; for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, place something on top which will calm it down.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the ear in the hand (i.e. a type of swelling or inflammation).
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The vertebrae that arise in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is a part where there are bones, and sometimes there is an angle, and one of them arises at the root of the joint, or the birthmark is on some of the vertebrae.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born in any part of the neck or shoulder do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the shoulder may possibly move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut on a fat person is light, thusly:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it in its root with a wide scapula-shaped instrument.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born in the root of the joint is grievous to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	if it clings, do not cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that who is born or swells in the last notch, it is necessary that you cut around the flesh up to the bone first, then cut the bone with a string suitable for that, then dress it until it be healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that occurs on the fingers together comes from birth, or a boil, or scorching by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is fitting that you cut the suture, so that it can be repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or moistened cloths soaked in rose oil, so they do not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin wooden splints, until the place is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling occurs on any of his fingers with the palm, cut out that swelling in the way it is necessary.
des vils	of evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Boils are swollen, inflamed, and full of melancholy fluid that occur in several members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to them occasional purging with vinegar, and then heal the boil with balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron cauterization is according to two manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that one strikes them and scrapes off the dark blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you heat the vein, and scrape it all clean.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The incision is according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first take a sharp and very hot knife, until the large vein is thinned out, then restrain the patient's leg from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then uncover the vein in position I or II or III with a wide cut, then lift and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient's constitution can suffer.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and command him that he eats flesh in a thin broth with black vinegar.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and purging when the veins are full, and harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The relief of the body is in this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	lift the leg of the patient, if it has much hair, then put him in a bath, and rinse the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and swell the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat him by the fire, and then cut in the place of the vein near the long part at the knee, or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then prepare the skin with oil, and scrape off the flesh from each side until it feels tender when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then insert the rod underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then pour oil on it lightly, then bind it in another place with three threads.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin above the vein until it feels tender, then lift it up on the rod, as you have done, and anoint it with another oil, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then bind another strip, or more if you need them, then lift it up, and bind it to the middle of the foot, then pull and lift just to the second strip;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull it from strip to strip, until it comes out completely, then bind it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot pull it out and lift it, so put an awl on a very strong doubled thread, and bind and pull it, and put under the skin, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not splinter, for if it does splinter, then one cannot pull it out or lift it, and harm will come to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have pulled it all out, so put moist wool on the place of the wound in vinegar and rosate oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is twisted and distorted together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it unevenly, but do not splinter it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and pull it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one opens the vein is curved, and does not cut; so that it may open it.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of great curvature, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the thighs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry earth.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and perhaps it occurs elsewhere than in the thighs, and this happens due to the rotting that comes from beneath the skin, just as snakes and worms breed inside the body between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this inflammation are such that it comes to the leg a great swelling; then the place changes and the inflammation begins to come out, just as a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the joint opens, you should wrap it around with a piece of linen cloth that is one and a half ells in length up to II [i.e. two-thirds of an ell], and then tie the knot, and let the linen stay on the leg, and every time it slips out, wrap it around again with the linen and tie the knot.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part of it, and wrap up the remaining part, and do not cut it in its root until it has come out completely;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, then it goes into the flesh and causes an abscess and putrefaction in its place, and a bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of this thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remain in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and at times this vein is treated when it is two or three palms in length, and a hand once came to me that had come out of it ten palms long, and when you cut it, so be sure to sew the edges together, and perforate down to the bottom, so that everything comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and let the matter that is inside be emptied out, and apply to the place medicines which prevent putrefaction for any day, then cure it just as abscesses;
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And at any time there are many veins, and indeed when it opens in the joint of the foot, or on the foot, and a lot of pus comes out, and from which it pours blood;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	cure then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This illness is called in our land "bovine disease", because it has happened many times in cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body rising and descending, and it feels bad as it travels from member to member, until it bursts out of the skin where it goes, and spurts forth.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is generated from corruption of some fluids, such as those that come from worms and serpents and lice and ascarids in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps entering in, and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and it happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him being cured and treated, one cannot escape the fact that he suffers.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so then you must bind the place above and below with a strong tightly fastened ligature, then cut up and remove it, and if the abscess is deep in the flesh, and you cannot find it, burn it with fire on top until it bursts;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that he does is that he makes people go blind, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, bind a loop under it tightly, then cut up and remove it;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and the patient needs to be cleansed of bodily impurities with solvent medications for the bad humors that are ailing him, and he must avoid rank meats causing corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from windness (or indigestion)
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land; it is a pain that comes to certain members, and moves from member to member.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I see what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to an ill woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I saw it rise also like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like bright silver when it cuts from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later ran through all the body, so that it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was twisting around the body, as I had seen it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it moved from member to member, because I had never seen this illness in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I have often thought that the pain had moved from one place to another well, but I did not see it, as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought it was because the woman had a thin body and her veins were revealed, and for this reason that appearance of windiness constrains;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear according to this reason in those who are corpulent and have moist bodies and veins that are well-concealed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see to cure this illness and the patient feels that pain, if it becomes apparent as we have said, then lay a bandage above and below hastily, and then cut above so much that the windiness constrains itself back into place.
et cauterize le leu;	and apply fire to the spot;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see to it yourself, then have the patient be treated by those who purge windiness, such as fetid pills and serpent pills and similar others.
des saiettes	from arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Splinters are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The differences of them are that there are those with large points, small ones, hairy, and studded.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those who have two angles, and of those with tongues, and of those where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which drops in any member as it does in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal member it drops, such as brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it drops then in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, warn you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then it is necessary that you beware of extracting this arrowhead, for death follows in many conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this evil sign does not warn you at all, and the arrowhead is not deep within, then draw it out, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes it and penetrates the bone, and the skull vein that is above the brain bursts, is when there is scotoma and hotness and sweat and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and commotion of understanding, and vomiting of gall.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perchance it lacks force from the nostrils, or the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps the speech and voice are impaired;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is a discharge of a white moist wound that looks like pus, and also as if it were burned charcoal;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, take care of the treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is not already out;
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it pierces or enters into the heart are that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in a hard thing, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perchance the arrow moves as pus does, and in cutting black blood, and there comes coldness and cold sweat, and syncope;
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know for certain that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the splinter that never leaves the spleen is that a foam bursts out from the wound and the throat swells up, and the patient's skin turns color, and they gasp high and cry for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow pierces into the covering of the liver, it will be near the little ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	And pours out great pain and great suffering; and sighs;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the splinter falls in the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat bursts out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow sticks in the stomach and jumps into the intestine through a hole, then there is no hope for treatment nor extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if an arrowshot goes into the bladder, and the urine shoots out and comes forth, and the patient feels a great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arm and neck and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and forearm and elbow and knee and toes and the limbs similar to them, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, therefore do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man whose arrow shot into the eye at the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and led it out in another direction under the fat of the ear, and it was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And pulled out from the eye of a man with an arrow that had shot into the fat under the paper which is behind it, and the arrow was bent back, and could not be drawn except for the tip towards the bowstring, and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow, all made of iron without feathers.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The game was sutured, and no bad accident came to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with earrings:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I removed the barbs, and smoothed it out as much as I could until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled an arrow from under the house, that had lodged in his belly, and I thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then since he passed 30 days, it did not change its condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrowhead and sewed it in, and drew it out, and he had no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whom an arrow has fallen on his back, and the wound is sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and it did not change its natural condition, nor found any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And behold another man, to whom an arrow was shot into his face, and the wound was sewn up.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And the king's servant was struck by an arrow in the neck, and he was slightly leaning to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow had been completely repelled.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat him after it had been three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched her completely in a subtle tent, and I didn't find anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and hurt beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow I put on the wound a poultice attractive and digestive, because the place did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I appeared to the seat of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the poultice many times a day, and solved the wound again, and the patient remained in this way for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day deep inside his body.
et il le me dist.	and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied to the wound a corrosive medicine by many days, until it was open and I tried and felt the head of the arrow which was protruding at the place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted into the opening of the wound by that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became visible to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and the arrowhead passed well through the terminations in four months, and then it loosened so much that I put forceps into the wound, and pulled out from one end and the other, and could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then I did not cease to subtlety and ingeniously examine methods of instruments, until I took it one day with well-made forceps, according to the shape that will come at the end of this chapter, until I extracted and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the expert judges that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I've told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your treatment on what I don't say at all, for books cannot possibly contain everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but wise masters learn from a small thing well done, and on what is now present and defective, they find new work, and new instrument, at the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not emerge from limbs where they are stuck except in two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they entered, or on the other side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that one which jumps out through there where it enters is an arrow entering into fleshy places and jumps out at once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, then let it be left for as long as the flesh is putrid around it and let the exit become swollen;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then let it be left thus for some days and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps out, and if it does not jump out, then perforate around with a fine point so that the place around it is enlarged, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes just up to one of the cavities of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said occur to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If you do not pull it out, but leave it so that it is even after a few days, since the arrowhead comes to just so close to the skin, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone itself and does not come close to the skull, and the patient remains for a few days without bad accidents, then one should think about pulling it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very tightly inserted and cannot come out easily, then I administer thorns around it, as I told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the place until it is sound.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrowhead is reset in its place inside the body and one cannot see it, then question him about every part.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead and there is no vein or nerve or artery, then cut it until the wound becomes large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to which it holds, remove the flesh that is stuck in there from both sides as far as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and take care to break the arrowhead carefully, so as not to bend it too sharply.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out once, leave it until the surrounding flesh is corrupted, then pull it out, for the extraction will be made clear.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding occurs contrary to what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting into the nerve and vein, and devise a plan by which you can draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and set the patient in the form that he was when the arrow hit him, for this is the greatest aid to be done, and if you cannot, then set him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or it pierces something out of itself, or the skin is swollen in the spot where you can see or feel it pulsing.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut then above, so that the pincers can take hold of it, and then draw it out.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If the bone jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand around gently, so that it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then let her wait a bit longer and begin to extract again until it comes out now.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is still in it, push it all the way into the shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft breaks, and you see fit to administer treatment, then administer the instrument with hair, so that the tip of the arrow goes into the hair of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push it out, and if the arrow is broken, then put the instrument with a pointed end in to loosen the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut out all of the flesh around where the poison is, if possible; then heal the wound as it is proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is in the loin or belly or bladder or side and it is close to coming out, and you can see it, then cut;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then close the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and let it heal until it is sound.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tongs used to pull out arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And they occur in many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, small, and medium-sized, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrow's fletching is also like the feathers of a bird, to guide it at the point of the arrow, as in this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pushing and knowing if it fits thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	arteries of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of the veins from which one takes blood are 31, of which there is chief 16, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	the two vessels behind the ears, which are called "herbech".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two apparent temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the inner corners of both eyes, which are called "aspires".
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the veins that are at the back of the neck;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are in the throat.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on top of the lips above the mouth, and they are called "augheherich".
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and there are two veins under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly used for bleeding are V-shaped in each arm.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein and it is to be found on the left side of the chest, and they call it the common people "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "fast" and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it the common people "vein of the heart".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic vein is to the right side and they call it the common people "vein of the belly", and it lies over the armpit, and it is that one which bleeds and shows itself clearly above the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the Salvette vein is the vein that lies between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	And there are three veins in the leg and foot:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is under the prominence of the left sock's side, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle of the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "nisse", which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The sweating of the veins that are behind the ears helps against catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the sweating, as I told you, is that you raise the head of the patient and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then press the patient's neck with a vice, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places of the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Heat the needle then to your shoulder, and where you feel the hair under your shoulder, if it is inflamed.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet, and stick it through under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand to all the vein upwards, and cut and the skin and the vein well two fingers deep, and make blood come out as far as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then hold it tight and bind, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The bleeding of the two arteries which are in the two temples, is worth for an old migraine, and soreness, and accustomed to blindness of the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the bledder if it is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient strains his neck so that the two veins appear clearly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and send a servant with the hair on your head, to sign up for it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the needle on top of the vein high up at your head's index, and push in the lancet below, and lift the vein upwards, and cut it, just like you did with two other veins, and make the bleeding stop according to your necessity.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your hand on top of the vein for one hour, then put a cotton cloth on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then bind her tightly, and let it be until she is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken about their cutting and extraction, and of the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is worth just as much as the phlebotomy to the cephalic vein in ancient face diseases, and in migraine, and in epilepsy.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient twists his neck, so much so that a vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and put the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and let two drops of blood come out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein so tight it is well sealed, and one should work without a broad gauze.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not necessary that the bandages be too tight;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the stitches come undone crosswise, because the bone is close, and by chance break the bandages when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The stitching of the two veins that are in the armpits is helpful to both eyes, and to the itch, and to the redness, and to the erysipela in the eye, and to the ailments of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting at any ligature, so to speak;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then it bleeds, and the blood is dark, as long as a piece of flint that is somewhat wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the blood flows subtly, perhaps it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then apply linen to the blood, as much as you need, and then bind on cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The blood of the vein of the neck is worth as much as a fever, and a severe headache, and face diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient strains his neck, then strains his head to your left hand, and take out the subtle long blood, and place it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start to flow now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep into profundity, and make a compress of cloth over the blood according to your need, then bind it for one night, for it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The poultice of the two strings is very helpful for the constriction of an abscess, and in the beginning of ulceration, and in many diseases, and in swelling, and in corroding, and in herpes, and in ulcers;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the poultice is that the patient tightens their neck under one and then the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the surgeon being above the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a seat, then they bleed the long vein a little wide, then drain the blood temperately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then remake another part in the other vein, then release the ligament, and hold it loosely with moderate force, so that the patient does not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let him alone until morning, so that the wound be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the salve of books (note: this seems to be a phrase or term being used in this text)
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins on the upper lips is said to help against sores in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cracks in the lips, and around the neck.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of healing is to have the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, of which one is on the right cheek and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the small black threads around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	therefore cut one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest vein from each side, and make the two veins that are above and below in the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the treatment under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The vein bloodletting that is under the tongue helps afterwards in the head bleeding, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and the illnesses of the eye, and the illnesses of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient sees between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up their tongue, and looks under them on each side a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then bleed one and then the other, and do not go too deep, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck from which we commonly bloodlet are bled in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with a very fine needle, as cutting threads, or olive-like subtle points, and it is called "anequil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is very well known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It is necessary to open the veins filled with thick blood visible on the surface, and that contain thick blood and turmoil.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it is the form of a flamelike olive leaf:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is finer when pointed, and is for healing fine veins, or where there is fine yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The sap of the basil plant, which is one of these veins, does service to the illnesses that are under the throat, and around the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the sap to flow freely, and that he be careful of the artery which is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a great flow of blood comes out, then it is necessary to bind it, as I said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and it must not be grasped by the flamelike part, but cut off like a piece of wood.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the sap of the basil plant does not appear visibly, then it is necessary that you extract it, and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	Where you want to draw blood from him, or if you are to bind it up with a ligature on his arm.
elle apert manifestement;	it is opening up obviously;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the cauterization with fire to the surface, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you stretch out his arm, so that you touch the place as long as you recognize the hairs;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with ink and then bind the arm, and cauterize the vein with fire anew.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and beware that you do not cut in the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is of the artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it coming out as high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood of the artery:
