haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten yourself then, and put your finger on lengthily; then take out your finger if the blood has stopped, for it often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Let the arm remain so, and do not move it, the patient.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be on guard, and do not move it until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood is not stopped, and it bleeds, and medical treatment is not present, then cut the artery if it shows, for the head of the vein will recede.
et estainche li sans.	and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bark of vitriol, and tear it, and take one half and bind on well up to the other side.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the bleeding is stopped, that's good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then cure it as we have said with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and stitches are not put in many positions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein of the neck in a middle position so helps that it treats blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephatic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the vein person to be cautious about the nerve that is below, and if he pricks too deep, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the stitches become inflamed, and perhaps cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve opens up very often, and if it does not open in some humans because of its subtlety, then you must not tie the stitches with the instrument anew.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and spare the nerve at your will.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there are veins between the two nerves, then cut them long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The purging of the cerebral vein helps, which draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to purify by piercing with a fiery olive or a fiery myrrh, for this is the most safe of all veins, because it does not pass under the nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter position and do nothing if we fail the first time, and then begin again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the places swell in some men when we fail the first time, but it does nothing harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of healing is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about purging is that purging is not done forcefully except to keep health and to prevent illnesses from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the purging be done in one of the three veins that are or cut:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	It is to know, cephalic, facial, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it is necessary to bleed at the beginning of spring and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one must bleed either the first day or the third, after 2 hours or 3 days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding which is administered to the sick does not have a fixed hour determined, but when need arises by day or night, at all hours and in all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to bleed children until the age of XIV years, nor a woman carrying fruit more than two quarters of the month up to seventh [month];
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should old people who have passed 60 years be healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to bleed, however it is done, it is necessary that he cleanse the intestines with a light clyster, if there are many bad humors retained, so that the veins do not draw out of the intestines the superfluous things that are hurtful to the main members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	He who is too full of meat, nor one who is drunk, as long as he remains so, nor a dropsical person;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and they are not to be healed after an acute colic has passed, and vomiting, and evacuation of the belly, and frequent intercourse with a woman, and excessive toil, wakefulness, and fasting, and everything that overcomes either virtue or physical strength;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly purge the humours, if the blood is thick, by means of meat and drink and medicine, if you have the power to do so;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then let him enter a bath, unless some thing prevents it, to subtlety evacuate the blood, and so heal the flux of the vein around the navel by the third part, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and let him guard that day from toil, and pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be seated and quiet, and let the nurse sit higher than he who is to be nursed, and stroke the arm twice or thrice, then gently pull out the string from above, for when it is too tight or loose, so that blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then stroke the place with hands until the veins swell, and check with them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the nurse's flame with a spoonful of old oil, then place the tip of his left hand on top of that vein near the place to be bled, so that the vein does not flow and burst when cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flow as quickly as strings when being let, and some of these are so full of windiness, so that when the flame is placed on them, they draw back into themselves, and cannot be opened, and thus one must be wary of such.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it bleeds excessively, then the wound is too narrow, so it behooves the surgeon to be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, that's good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, it restarts again a little below that place or on top hastily, if the place is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is swollen and the patient becomes frightened, leave it alone for one or two days and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps a pus-filled swelling will come;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not let him enter the bath, then restart the surgery if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, cut the vein finely and you doubt that it does not bleed as much as you see, then close in on that same opening directly with all the flaming.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and do some work with a poultice, so that the place may be inflamed.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	if you see the place inflamed, do not reapply the salve, and put on a poultice of linseed oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and is soothing in this place with a calming effect like oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the linseed oil for every salve that you apply to veins in order to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and it is the same with egg white and butter, when one puts them on the place.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	when the blood oozes out and separates if it is too much.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a big abscess which often happens, especially when the wound is not fully healed from that time or the opening of the vein is small, you hurry and put on the place a sponge wet in water and tied with hot thread, and hold it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the bleeding from the vein, and if he remains in place for some days with no blackness or greenness, then it does not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on some thing of aloes or myrrh dissolved in vinegar, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times an abscess and appearance of pus occurs at the base of the scapula.
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	put then your hand on it, and if you find that place soft to the compression of the hand, it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Be careful then not to put on any of those things which we have said, for it may cut short the artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make him an unguent with a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until he is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each type of blood according to its quantity and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	If the blood is black, let it come out until it is red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see that the pus is thick, let it drain until it becomes subtlety or clearly;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is fat and strong, and needs the extraction of blood, that a larger wound be made, and the flaps be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it must be healed quickly and often, and it should be healed by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing saves from hemorrhage and cutting of the nerve, and is worth more than the healing by a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to one whose body is failing at the wound site, it is necessary to give him moist bread in vinegar of lemons.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is overheated, have him take three or four bleedings of blood. And if he has a cold complexion, have him take medicine before the purging potion with moistened bread in sweet syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it spouts to the vein, after the issuance of much blood, it is necessary that it inhale broth of meat, and a sweet-smelling syrup, and use other things which we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to evacuate his arm and heal another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great surgery, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue, continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to evacuate his arm after the first surgery, and he has a strong body, should heal in 7 hours after the first surgery, or after the 9th hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to be healed from another side, should be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For he has much blood inside the body which is already overheated, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to let out a great quantity, and to enlarge the wound so that it becomes as big as a palm.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you will reward all the signs of health, and place your hand over the sores when they heal, lest death comes in place of healing, and such things happen many times, when the surgeons are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see the arm being released, and blood coming out a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press hard on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If he is bent, let him stretch out his arm hastily, for it would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him leave it alone until he heals the second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you shall prick at the tip of the flame, until the blood that is congealed in the vein issues forth, and put on a poultice made from water and pressed upon lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, let it be alone and do not bind it tight until the inflammation has calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to let blood again the second time, then heal it in the same place, or in another wound, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The wound on the arm is healed in that place instead of the wound of the head because it is complicated.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is that the patient shall put his hand in hot water until the scab be red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it must be tied moderately, so that the vein appears well, then let him heal now from across, not from the width or length;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and it should be made wide, and let him heal well near the joint of the hand, and if there is no blood coming out, then put his hand in hot water, and let the blood clot in the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in winter, do not rub the hand with hot water, for it puts it more in cold than in winter;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this wound is safer from all other wounds, with no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the salivation on the right hand is worth to all diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	hold the hand and put it in hot water, as long as the vein will be visible, if one sees it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein crosses over, and you cut from top to bottom entirely, it hurts nothing;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deep into the flesh, for the nerves are all hidden under naked bone, and then put the hand in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as much as it's necessary for you to let, then put on the swelling oil and bandage to bind quickly, and thus do with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The swelling on the left hand is worth the sickness of the gout, and do with it just as I told you to do with the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sores of the sophene are worth for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the loins, and retention of flower (perhaps "flowers" referring to blood vessels?), and disease of the kidneys, and hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of his health is such that the patient puts his foot in hot water and scrapes over the vein as long as it burns, and lies over the jointure of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	treat then the most swollen vein, or that of the ankle, which is most valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and the treatment crosses also as when cutting;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flame be unsteady.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood can't come out, then put the foot back in the water and let it bleed well out of the swelling.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the cauterizer fails the first time, then he recommences the second above a spot, for the place is salted;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	nor doubt of nerves, as we have said, and so do the same on the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic swelling is at the knee of the back leg, and its abscess is worth the pain in the back when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his health is such that the patient enters or bathes and stretches four fingers above the ankle by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then let him bleed in all ways that you can, and crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	it is worth noting that you should not cut it, for the place is swollen, and it has healed too quickly in the space of several hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then bleed any vein that opens from the back of the foot and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and do so much bleeding as you see, and then loosen the string, and put on a compress and bind it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	venous bleedings by suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Venesections are made from horns, or copper, or glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and a purging by vomiting is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by cutting and attracting blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this purging which is without cutting is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is with hot drink, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and purging which is done by cutting and extracting blood is done in 14 places of the body, from whom one is entirely under the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is on the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the poultice under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the poultices on the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the poultices above the kidneys;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the poultices in the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the poultices on the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping of both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cupping does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore one must not weaken them at all, as is done with vein-cutting;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, nor with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from over-fullness, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it is necessary to cup because of diseases or for custom, then we must administer each one an hour at the beginning or end of the month, and in between and at every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are such people who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are such people who find fullness and redness in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darkness around their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and are bleeding;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are those who suspect, and see through the blood and wounds and deaths and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and indeed when it is in the middle of the month, let us command that they be bled after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The discharge from the mouth so helps with the looseness of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not fitting that this should be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this purging so is in place of the discharge from the head, and it is not fitting that he who has a cold complexion uses it, or who has cathartic, for it does them much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and because of this it is not fitting that the old people use it, nor those who have cold illnesses in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed themselves, become forgetful, and for this reason the cupping glass should be placed a little lower on account of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The purging in the throat is in place of the discharge from the head and of the apoplexy, and because of this it is worth it for the constriction of the belly, and the rupture of the channel of the womb, and all, and fullness;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to press hard, for if it holds too tightly, there will be dislocation or damage to the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The hiccups of the two costal bones under the neck are worth the pains in the head, and dimness and migraine, and suffocation, and the pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is a sign of the sickness of the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you must instruct the surgeon to stretch out his hand to put it in, that he not strike the artery and cut off blood flow suddenly.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The hiccups under the chin are worth a disease of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is a sign of the sicknesses of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The bloodlettings on the shoulders are worth for illnesses that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The hiccups of the ribs are worth as much as the three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon not to cut too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh and knows underneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping vessel that is on the buttock is worth for hemorrhoes from the foundation, and for diseases underneath, and it must be large, and made of brass, so that it needs to be well squeezed;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it were thin, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Cupping vessels of the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from all the body, and are worth for ancient pains in the reins, and for gout, and for the bladder, and remove the boils.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are in place of the two kneecaps, and the two ankles, and although they weaken the body after long use, and cause a faintness in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to put the ventouse is that you put it first empty, and suck temporally, and put hastily, and move evenly, and do not cease from doing this, so long as you see the red place swell and appear with reddening of blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then apply heat, and put on the ventouses, and take note of the position of the body, for there are such who have thick flesh, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	it is necessary to cut once only, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a few deep ones;
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to cut twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time in order to subtily make a way for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to cut the third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out a little blood bit by bit, if we suffice with just one time.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, then we recommence often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, then fire it up thoroughly, and the ends should be pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for one with tough skin and hard flesh, and who have prominent pores, that you grease the places of the cupping glasses with oily purifying and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is with esteem, with violet oil, or with sweet almond oil, or with cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is with rue, with plantain oil, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or of balm, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person who is being treated has tender skin and large pores, then there should be no oil put on it, but rather it should be washed after venesection with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or melon seed water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, should rise with ass's milk, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities arise from old wine, or from vinegar of wormwood, or from the decoction of rue or chamomile, or something similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it is not advisable to treat with a poultice before bathing or in a bath, but after the bath for an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is not advisable to sleep after the poulticing, and it is necessary that he be washed, when he must be poulticed and when he is poulticed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are sick with a choleric temperament, and whose blood is too hot and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that he take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in broth, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and mutton soup, and beef from the loin, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, should take honey syrup, and medium wine that is between old and new, and mutton soup, and mutton broth, and young fowl and small pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day when he will sweat, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people treacle or muscatel before sweating, or afterwards, in order to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be thinned, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The poultices that are put on without hurting are those that are put on the liver, and the spleen, and gout, and the belly and the navel and the groin and the thigh, for these members do not tolerate being hurt there, and one only does it in order to draw blood from member to member, as we put them on the breasts when the milk comes out;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put poultices on the belly and on the navel to reduce the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And it takes away pain, when there is a splinter or stone, so by its attractive virtue it happens that the splinter is taken out, or the stone is removed from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and similarly it does when it is applied to the liver and the spleen when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty so that they suck only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together fire, and sometimes mixed with hot vinegar, such as in the malady of the pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with warm vinegar or with vinegar that has been cooked with herbs convenable to these things.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the plaster administered on fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be two fingers wide and a half palm deep, and there should be around the middle a small pit, as when one is to prick with an awl, and it should be of lead, soft in front so that it does not wound the patient when put on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And it should have a staff of about one mile in length made of bronze or iron to carry a candle enclosed, and there should be large and small ones according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for children's cupping glasses are different from those of adults, and thin ones for the lean and fat ones for the plump.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And so one should put this cupping glass above the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the candle made of tallow or linen, and put it inside the cupping glass at the length of the staff that is in the cupping glass, so that the light may be at the bottom of the cupping glass and not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and you should be above the spot that we said, so that when one wants, if the vapour goes out, take off the cupping glass.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and mark with ink as before, and repeatedly re-mark it if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass which is administered in illness of pleurisy, with great heat, it does not have a stick or a hole, and it is only applied when it is full of water, and it is placed on the member only.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction cups are only applied when one cannot put a cupping glass on account of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare places without fat, such as elbows or knees, and others similar.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of suction is that when you find cups that are in sweet clear waters with a sense of bubbling, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them into fresh water until they are familiarized and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleansed with wine and a bird's beak [a type of surgical instrument], then rub the limb until it is red, and apply vinegar.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are smooth and hardened, if it is place where a bird's beak can be applied, then put one there, because that will help a lot afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then raise the place with a spoon and then with a sharp knife, very well, and then bind it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place becomes too swollen with the vinegar, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the swelling is decreased.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the swelling is multiplied, then apply vitriol dissolved [or] galena and similar things, until it is decreased.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put half of peeled peas on the place, and leave them until they dry out to the place, which will now stop it.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more thread, take other suture.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the sutures do not want to take hold, soak the area with fresh blood, and then insert a needle until the thread comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are coming undone, powder on a little bit of aloes and linen thread, or ashes, so they will hold now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of wounds (or "The Book of Bruises").
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for wounds and swellings.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Learned doctor, know that foolish men have fallen from this chapter, which never saw the ancient books, nor read a letter about it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of that reason is estranged the science in our land, for I never found one good;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing else, except by the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated with science and by experience, and by the habituation of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have thus described in this chapter that which is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of instruments that are brought to bear, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So then it is fitting that we say the prologue of this book, which are the summaries of words and chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been proven wise may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that whenever a break or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient from one part and then, if nothing else prevents it, as weakness of body, or childbirth, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the temperature is too hot, or too cold.
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and have him drink cold broths, that is to say, cold joints, and the flesh of hare and goat, and let him not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill him with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you are in doubt about a hot abscess or an effusion of matter into the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient recovers by first-class management which they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make thick nourishment, or have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and eggs, and peas, and veal, and oysters, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the flesh is repaired more quickly and the wound heals sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones broken in old people and those who are decrepit cannot be well reunited or soldered according to their nature for the weakness of the members, nor can those which are too soft, such as those of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no cure, remove the splint from the broken bone and bind the large linen strips which are dry and join the limb together so that it becomes strong again as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not take him away from his work, and for this reason he must be nourished with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that wounds are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the wound of the head is one thing, and the wound of the back or leg is another, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of wounds.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are wounds that go around an arm or leg, and others that cut into it, such as the cut of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And also wounds with an open gash, and wounds with a small slit or tear.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in each case let his device and his proper instrument be at hand in the restoration, according to what has been remembered by him.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the fracture of the bone is because the place is twisted and opens well on the outside, and sounds to the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no tortuosity nor sound in the joint, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may well have tortuosity, or a split, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So do not move the hand, but put on medicines that come later, and then bind it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks that go inwards and are the two parts separated, you must now set them back to the same point, so that the swellings come into being.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the swellings come, leave it alone for a day, until the swelling is calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it back in place with a needle that you can easily and cleanly push through, and know that the restoration of a joint is easier than restoring one where there are fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it firm, as it should be thus afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken fragments, if it is an arm or leg, or if at your hand it is a small member, or with two strings, or with one string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member in its natural shape; so that when the parts of the broken member are set straight, then reset with all kinds of instruments the dislocations in their places as quickly as you can, and ensure that through your work no harm or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join the two bones of the joints together properly according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if you think it is not good.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if it settles well and is not strained too much or pressed as those who do it by their work bring abscess to heat and contraction in the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is ready, then punish the patient so that he does not move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the member be so secure that the patient feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	When he feels no pain, it is not entirely so, and he must be placed in such a condition that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and he is kept in order to make sure it is set straight, so twisting does not occur when he is reset;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the shape of the broken limb should be according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as wrists and elbows and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is necessary to envelop with a linen cloth that is soft and delicate.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those which are large, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is necessary to envelop with a linen band that is wide and strong, for the broad bands encircle all the large limb and hold it from all sides equally, so there is no tearing.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around the stoppers light ones, three turns or four according to the limb, and hold with your hand a peg at all the band, then go above the break and restrain less, so that the break will move away one peg from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the string little by little, as long as you take a large part of the healthy place, then take up the other string and turn it around again over the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the break and hold it moderately, not too hard nor too gently, as we have said in the first line above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the strings some pads of linen or cloth until it is entirely even, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put on your well-made splints, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then put on something soothing and hot that removes the swelling, and leave it like this for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then tighten the splints above and be of half the width of a well-sharpened cane or of wood from which we make knives, or of palm tree sapwood, and be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the splint put on the break is a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as is necessary for the limb of smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind on the splints just like you did at the first joint, then tie above with a cord gradually, just like in the first joint over the break;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is above, the looser it becomes;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the cord be middling, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the cord is thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their stitches with linen threads twisted in error, and it's a great mistake, for the stitch cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two fingers' breadth between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the splints' ends after being bound in their healthy places, then put under them linen wrappings or torn flannel, so that they do not become worse.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the skin is torn, I will tell you the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not need to bind with splints all broken members at first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	When the member is great, there should not be put a poultice unless after 9 or 7 days, or more according to your security against hot suppuration;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and behold here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that stands by the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundant egg juice, and put this concoction, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring breakage in many dispositions, and indeed for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of plaster restoring breakage and dislocation and twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take 3 parts of balm and linseed oil and onycha and gum arabic and myrrh, mix it ten to three.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Myrrh and aloe, each five times;
alechil VIIII З.;	Aloe eight times;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into powder, and mix with the marrow of an egg.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another manner of plaster that is useful against twisting;
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take myrrh and balm, each ten times;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Myrrh and aloe, each nine times;
acaice VI З.;	Gallnuts six times;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Armenian balm ten times, and pound it well, and mix with vinegar or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another manner of plaster for joints and broken bones out of their places, and eases the pain beforehand, and the surgeons use it for splints and breakage;
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new linen cloth, and moisten it with warm oil and melted lard, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not cure [it], but they are good for calming a hot abscess, and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another manner of plastering that cures broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	take dried leaves of fig and wild marjoram, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster for the repair of a crack in the bone and to reduce the remaining part of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of vervain, chamomile, flowers of violets, wheat flour, one part from each.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and mix with wine, and if the member is hot, mix with moisted water of coriander or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of applying ointment more strongly than the first, when a hardened abscess comes to restoring the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of vervain, and seeds of flax, balm, marjoram, hyssop, and flowers of violets and chamomile, one part from each.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and mix with salt water or sweet water or with wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates says that for the restoration of a broken member, one should only use a wax made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between soft and hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that for the restoration of a broken member, one should put on things which are slightly hot and dry, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another manner of plastering that is good for lesions and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	take moss and hazel nuts that are split in two, or quills of birds, and plantain, and sew them together evenly, and pound them, and make a plaster from it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen the plaster a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone returned to its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if you do not loosen it by hand within days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, with much rest or inflammation, then hasten and loosen it, and remove the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take light cloth and moist sea sponge, and plunge it in water, and lift up the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then apply a wet compress of linen soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it with a cloth until you are certain of warm abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and keep the inflammation from affecting the member, and may it be taken away the pain, then repeat the subtle binding, and a little plaster, and do not strain it so hard as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and bind it subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the swelling is gone, and redness and pain and inflammation have ceased entirely, and you need to apply a poultice and binding again, so do it again, as you did first treatment.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing comes to the member of what we have said, then do not remove the binding until after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and every time let it rest for twenty days, according to what we see, until the fracture is sound, and the approximation of the bone to the flesh on.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then the swelling increases more than before, and the meat of the flesh becomes inflamed, as I said beforehand.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the place drying out more than is necessary, know that inflammation will not come;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	take hot ironed thread then every third day, and soak a piece in it;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work the inflammation is cut from the member, and hastily correct what foolish surgeons do that leave the member twisted;
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is evil, and it is a fearful work, and I see nothing else but to bind tightly and to do things properly;
des diverses manieres de brisure	It seems like the text has switched to a new topic. The phrase "des diverses manieres de brisure" can be translated to "of various types of bruising". This could be referring to different ways that people can experience bruising, or perhaps different methods for treating or describing bruises. If you'd like to share more context or continue with the translation, I'd be happy to help!
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	there are many manners of breaks, and various forms, and the causes are destined;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are breaks that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the arm breaks all the bone right up to the sycophagus which is under the bone, just as does an axe or a club;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and because of this it is called this manner of breaking "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Where the lance pierces through the bone above without piercing, and it is called this manner of breaking "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and it is a wound from these two breaks big or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow, or a fissure, or a bruise from a stone, or falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a bruise pressing, which approaches just to the skin that is under the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is closed in the bone as finely as a hair, and it is a small crack, and because of this it is called this break "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made either by being hit with a stone or by falling or by something similar, and makes the piece of bone fall downwards, and it is hollowed out like when blacksmiths heat up cauldrons.
si entre li piere dedens.	if the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to children who have soft bones in their head.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and occurs in all these kinds of breakage where small pieces are torn apart, as with them;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I shall speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of bruises by the swelling on them, and the inflammation that has been tested, and by the corrupt flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary bruise is known by this: when the bone is uncovered and you rub your finger on it, if the bruise opens up black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the bruise, be careful about the accidents that have befallen the patient. And if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of blood, loss of understanding, extension, palpitation, high fever, and the eyes coming out and becoming red, and other similar signs in more serious dispositions, then it cannot be healed with any doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it's in winter, it is fitting to remove the bone before the 14th day of the moon that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the 7th day, so that the flesh under the bone is not corrupted, and the accidents which we have spoken of come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the breakage of the bone comes up to the skin that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and that you take the patient's head and uncover above the bone in every way you can, and on the surface of the wound as gentle as you can, and if hemorrhage comes to reveal the bone or abscess appears, then help him with what is needed, and it is that you fill the place with moistened cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed down, and be sure of a cessation of bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One manner of treatment is that you apply to the narrow part in front, and this is its form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I insert a second swelling, one greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have various types of instruments, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and dense, you should pierce around it so that you administer instruments with awls, not too deeply that they penetrate beyond the bone of the test, and it should have above the tip a margin or circle, so that the point does not pass through the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it is necessary to have many of them, so that each comes in its proper place from the depth of the bone, so that you have awls for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three types of awls:
