Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing into the broken bone is that you put the awl on the bone, and turn to your fingers so much as you know the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put the awl elsewhere, a little after, and do this all around, then take the files to the space of the bone that is between the punctures, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, just as we have said, so much that you bring the bone into your hand, or onto any of the instruments you have such as forceps, pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and cleaned the bone, it is necessary that you sharpen the rasp that remains of the bone on all other instruments similar to an emery stone, but it must be sharper and more subtle than the other emery stone.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it remains of small bones, or no scales, then lightly break the bone with instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with ointments and unguents that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other manner of treatment is what Galen says, which is more safe.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he says it is very strong, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, in the place where the break shows clearly; so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place beneath the head of this incisional lens the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and the wound is sharp in two directions, so that the cutting is towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small mallet up above, so that you lightly cover the bone all around, and take good care of the skin that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhered to the bone, then lightly break it, for you break it very little harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce all the way to the tissue, and the bone is chiseled only so far that it leaves small pieces, then you should cover over that roughness and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you should have in various quantities, in order to smooth out each part as well as possible, according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you go before large rasps and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other cutting instruments and fine breaks, it is necessary that you bring cause according to its direction.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that has not been replied to by him who put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the blister is uncovered, then you must take a cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to harm the blister, then administer above the other bandage, and do not compress it too much that just until it soothes the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it thus for one day or two, until the abscess is calmed down, then loosen it, and administer medicine such as lily roots, and wheat flour, and incense powder, and Aristolochia, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make powder from these things, and apply it to the wound, and administer various medicines without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and make sure the wound is clean from then on, that you do not leave salve there, nor permit it to be stitched up, for when the edges of the skin meet over the flesh of the brain, they will swell and inflame, and the patient will suffer great harm.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one applies a caustic substance to the skin, it blackens over it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any evil accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if the blackening does not come that is due to the medicine you have put on it, with such virtue as it has, then you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix one draught in it, and apply it to the caustic.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure should be done by the ways that are required, until they are healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes are broken the two parts of the neck above, or one by itself, because they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that one below is cartilaginous and does not break if it does not get crushed or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you reset your little finger or perforation of the neck, and place this breakage even inside your index finger and in the palm outward, until the neck returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain by your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and you cannot reach it with your little finger, then you should put it back into place with a wooden mallet, not too big.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is of two parts, do it in the same way, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling of the abscess has eased, then reset at the head of the neck with a cloth made of linen, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you press on the other side, if there is a fracture there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and the tumors are so large that they fill the openings of the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some physician said that one must moisten the tents with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that it is well done, but they should be moistened with the mixture of aloe from egg whites, and flour.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tumor, until the bone is hardened and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never insert geese down into the nostrils in place of tumors, and if there is a soft cloth around it, and the fracture holds, and the patient breathes through it;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, put cerote or moistened cotton in rose oil or a small pouch of diachylon into the nostril.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess does not break out, apply an ointment in front of it with barley flour and incense powder, mixed with egg whites, then put on light bandages and do not bind down the nostrils.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the nose is small, and it has broken into small pieces, take it to suitable instruments for that, then sew up the breakage, and treat things that pierce through flesh, and soldering, as with suitable plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tentatives, and put poultices of clay on it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Il semble que nous avons changé de sujet !
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is out of place, and there is no wound above it, and the fracture is so slight that only, and not at all broken in two, forward than bent inward, then one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right side, that you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left jaw, then insert your index finger from the right hand, and press the breakage gently inside, and secure it with the other hand behind, and tie equally.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is split into two, it is necessary that you provide an extension of 2 inches by 3 inches until it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of the teeth has caused loosening or tearing, then bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk; then put on the broken jaw resin, and put on a bandage doubled over.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put on the patient a great bandage well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it up with a cord that you have, and instruct the patient to rest, and feed them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the face changes, then untie it on the third day, and then reset what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put ointment on it, of flour with abundance of egg or barley flour, after you have removed the grease;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on light wool ointment, and if the ointments are burnt, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until they are healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	It is often healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a boil or abscess appears, apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is break and wound together, repair that no part of the bone which has been taken out.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	with great subtlety of osteotomy with suitable instruments is advisable to those.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none left, sew up the wound if it is large, and put on one suitable ointment to prevent scarring, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fracture occurs in several places before the shoulder, and the breakage is according to three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and disjointed into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is thus when the fracture is without an open wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the fractured part feels.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches out the neck towards the affected area;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then set the break equal to your shoulders, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither swelling nor bulge.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend it further, place under the shoulder of the patient a round wooden or linen roll, and be as thick as your necessity requires;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and it is necessary to tie and loosen the ligature, and hold the probe in your hand, so that you place it equal with the break, as is fitting.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder blade out to the front because it is too deep, it is necessary that the patient lies on their back and places a middle bolster under their shoulder; then push the assistant down on the shoulder so that the bone of the shoulder blade is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then bring the break to your chest, and if you do not find any fragments, it is necessary that you split above.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and draw the pieces out lightly, and if the bone cannot join because of any obstruction, then cut with one of the knives that you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but put this instrument under the ligature to hold it in place.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and shape like a spoon, and is not sharp, and be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two holes, such as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, just as is the shape of the wound that you made when you drew out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of a hot abscess, then cut the wound, and if the ulcer is small, or you doubt it is a hot abscess, then cover the wound with linen and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the hot inflammation comes, you should soak a piece of linen in rose oil, garlic, and wine, and apply it to the wound.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The setting of a bone, when it is with wounds and cuts, is that you put on the bone the poultice of powder from the mill and of almond and egg white, and put on light cloths, and put a spear under the splint, if you need to.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide band of one palm in width, then put the linen cloth double on top of the cloths and poultice.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin bandage of three ells in width and length, and wrap it around that band so that the head of the band is hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put a bandage on the incision, and tie a cloth on the healthy shoulder, and under the healthy saddle, and under the sick saddle;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset it from each part, and when you see that the splint holds the incision properly, and you clearly see that the bandage does not move over the broken bone, then reward it each day, and when the stitches loosen, so hold it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and have the patient sit on his back, and put a small bolster under the saddle, to lift the shoulder high;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if it will lighten the dislocation of the shoulder by aligning the spine, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it until bad events come up, for twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then restart the poultice, if you see that it is necessary, and tighten and leave it so, until he is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and she is restored to health within twenty-eight days, and within less time than this for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	The shoulder breaks or loosens its place and does not allow movement; and it is known only by the feeling (or sense) of heat.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if you set it according to the shape of the break, and reset it in its natural form, in all ways that you know.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the place a powder of the mill with abundance of egg and light bandages, and put on a double cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put on a thin and delicate strap that is one pace further down from the shoulder than the strap, and under this strap there are hooks in no place of the shoulder; if you tie up this hair with strips of linen, so that the strap stays evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it tightly with a large bandage so that the strap does not move from its place, and inspect the binding every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time he relaxes, if it dislocates, then hold him firm and place the strap equal if it is out of its place, and have the patient lie on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder has been reset in twenty days or in twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is completed, if it dislocates, and be sure, for it is not bone that sets itself loose easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone sticks out and points under the skin, then take it up and draw it out, and do what we have said to calm an abscess or hot swelling.
de la brisure dou pis	Il semble que vous avez mentionné un autre type de blessure, celle du "pis" (probablement le poitrail ou le bassin).
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The thigh is sometimes broken in the middle, but this rarely happens.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it breaks often at the lower end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken inside, it slants downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks nourishment, and becomes thin, and by chance may vomit blood, and opens up the sinews in the broken bone, and they feel sick.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back and places an cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and gathers together the ribs of the two costal bones with your hands, and subtly do as you can to make them even in all ways until the shape of the bone is as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then apply ointments and bandages over the delicate steel needle of salt or other light wood, and enclose it in a linen cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the string back again to the back, and hold it firmly, and loosen each hour the ligature, and if it relapses, so restrain.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to untie because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, and clean the ointment, and address what has come from these ways of treatments.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the bandage, and hold it tightly until they are healed.
de la brisure des costes	C'est l'objet du texte que nous avions ! Le titre semble être une référence à un manuscrit médiéval qui traite de la fracture des côtes.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breakage of the ribs does not come from anywhere except in their large places after the back, and in the chest inside, and they do not bend more because they are greasy.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and he knows well beforehand the outcome of the investigation that he must undergo.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedy is that you set it straight again as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a poultice and bind with an iron band, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the break of the ribs is sloping inward, then the patient feels a very great pain and puncturing, as well as like a hiccough, for the bone pierces the flesh.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and it festers with pus, and boils and vomits great quantities of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancient ones have put in great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that it is necessary to administer foods which inflate the belly, so as to push the breakage outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot abscesses form there, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has already come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some of them said that one should apply cupping glasses to the place, so as to draw out strongly, and this seems to be in accordance with reason;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	nevertheless there is doubt that the cupping glasses may draw out the superfluities to the place because of its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And among us, one said that you should cover the place with wet wool soaked in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to put the linen back in its place, then treat it as if it were a case of pleurisy, meat wound, and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure because of the bone piercing the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to protect the spleen.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut into the bone and draw out lightly, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat them with poultices until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an abscess comes to a head, then put on damp cloths soaked in rose oil and apply them to the place.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat while the head of the abscess is still there what it needs to be treated with an opilasyon on the upper part where it should be until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a breakage occurs at the base of the neck bone and there comes a swelling.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also on the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, look closely and see if their hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and cannot move or stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when one holds them and pricks them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient has been cured, if a cure is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing occurs on the spine of the back and you wish to know if it is healed or not, then see if the vertebrae are softened, and if the parts that have been affected by the accident are in one's hands, and on the back there is windiness and excretion without will.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has cleaned it on their belly, then diarrhea occurs without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he lies on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that they are fatal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not labor much in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to them, the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you apply oil of rose or oil of marrow fat to it if there is a warm abscess, so long as it is appeased;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone has broken apart, it must be covered with the splint.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and cut out the bone, then close the two edges of the wound if it is large with a stitch, then treat it with ointment dripping with fat until he is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the bone of the shoulder is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", take your pouch from your left hand and place it equal to the other hand in your power, then apply the plaster and candle on top, if you need it.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then bind it, and if there is broken bone, do so on top, and apply the splint, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Here's a rough translation:
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Much often happens that the bone of the loin is broken, and if it does happen, there will be a small diminishment to the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and do two long ones, and go down by the shoulders, and come to the patient's pain at the joint, and prick, and swell what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand up, as high as you are above the break;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know what are the breaks and the shapes of them;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the break is in the head alone, set that break even, so that it is at natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is long, or it declines inside, then make the patient lie on their stomach, as much as the restoration of this breakage will become apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it even, put on the plaster, then put on a wooden or horn splint, and hold the break, so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and place the place under the ribs even, so that the ligature is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if a cold abscess comes, do not touch it until the cold abscess is quieted, and put on what we have said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then come back to the resetting, and hold it as is necessary, if there is no evil accident.
et c’est li maniere.	that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	La brisure de l'ajutoire (ou de la cuisse)
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joints are those which are between the cut and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of the two manners:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	Take a club made of plain ash tree, larger than this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And bind the two legs with two strings, and lift them up, and raise the patient on the seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then throw the broken arm over the club so that it comes to rest on the elbow, and have in the middle a support made of wood, then lift up onto some heavy thing or the servants stretch it down;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then place the splint equal to his hands together, so that the break returns as is proper.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one straps the patient on their bed, and ties their hand to their neck, then commands two servants to have one pull what is above the fracture to his hands, and the other to pull from below all the strings, and stretch each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then hold tightly to the strip below the cut and above it, and stretch each of the attendants to their share.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is close to the top of the shoulder, it is proper that you put the middle string under the elbow, and the other towards the armpit, under the splint;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the break is towards the armpit, it is proper to put the string lightly, without much effort, so that the break is even above the place and above the armpit;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then put equal the break, as it is necessary, and hold it, if abscesses are not coming to it.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses come to it, do not hold it at all until VII days, and put a linen cloth moistened in lard and rosed oil on it, as long as the abscess is appeased.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then hold it, and the manner of holding it is that you put the plaster on the break, then bring the arm up to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the bandage on it, and hold steady on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place of rest, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone is moved, use splints, and put on the break a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two spaces, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the break three fingers from each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then restrain on the joints, thus as I said at the beginning of this chapter on breaking, more strongly and less far apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the seat of the joints and the straining, as we have said, in the operation that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, so leave it to join just until the seventh day, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then look at each one every three days to the bandage, that itching or swelling does not come to it at the place, or the tightening does not come to the limb for it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the head of the arm, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents come to it, then do not remove the bandage until after three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back, and has his hands on his stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put under the aid one cushion made of wool evenly, and look every hour of the day or night whether the shape of the broken limb moves or the bandage becomes loose.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If he is treated by the virtue of medicine, and gives him food that we have put before, in such a manner that the food be at his first subtleties.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to recover, it should be coarse.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is custom that the shoulder and leg should be reset in forty days from then on;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must loosen him up and administer bath and ointment medicines to set the place right.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and stuck, then it stays to be untied for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus", one of which is small, and that is the bone that lies near the armpit.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and that is the one that is below, towards the little joint.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	perhaps break the large bone alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the little bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large ones are broken, then the healing is bad, and more serious than when they are broken all at once.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken only, then you must make a splint slightly extended and straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it's the great bone, so you have to hold it tighter;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it up to the chest, and lift the fold of the hand higher than the others, and the little ones lower than the others, and have the patient crossed over themselves, and the chest in front of them higher, so that the patient suffers no discomfort.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the assistant's arm to the part under their hand, or to his own thigh, and another assistant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the glass equally, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break there are pieces, then put each one back in its place, and if any is dislocated that you can't restore it to its place, then send for a surgeon, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with a break there is an open wound, I have spoken of it in the separate chapter;
si pren la cure.	If you take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of restoration a boil appears, take a poultice made from rose oil and white wax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and tie the poultice on top gently, until the boil is calmed down.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the wax and put on the plaster made from flour powder with a lot of egg white; then apply the stars, and let the star of the breaking be immediately stronger, and a little bit larger than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that he must have six arms or hands in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the breaking is in one of the bones, or in two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold more strongly above the breaking point than anywhere else, and always less far away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the dressings that are on the cut wound be soft and moist, and not hard or sharp;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and the string, by which he is restrained, should be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if some bad accident comes to the member, such as itching which comes to the member, then it is necessary that you anoint the member with hot water, until those itchings are calmed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member not tightly rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then reapply the stretching, and if the joint is loosened and the bone has become separated, and similar thing, then correct it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too narrow, then you should moisten it with one pess (i.e., a poultice) and let it be for some days until the swelling flows into it, and then tie.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not loosen him until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or inquire around it, then have him put his hands to his neck, and let his collars be equal, and he should beware of movement and agitation, and sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this cut wound is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty, according to the conditions and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and in its arm there occur many kinds of breaks, and it comes to be creased or bent many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the finger of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient crosses his legs and sits upright in front of him evenly.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place his hand on the stretched cloth and stretch out the splinted bones and set them straight with the mirror, until they are well aligned.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply the plaster and bandages, so that the swelling does not come, then put a stake according to the quantity of its place.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and it should be wrapped in an 'I' shape with linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is around the lower abdomen of the hand, make a roll with cloth and instruct the patient to hold it against his broken hand.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then hold it with a long cloth and the stick should be of good wood as large as the hand, and he will hold it, just as is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside, it is necessary that you put an iron band on top and another underneath in the wrist, so that the hand is open and straight; then tie all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the bones.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to any of us from above, then it is in the middle, then he puts it even, as it should be;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and bind with a plant and if you see that he puts in a straight small stake to lift the fracture and it does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the break is to other sides, such as in the index or one of the others, then he puts it even and binds with a sound ligature which is behind;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind them all together in one holding, as much as it is worth, or you put a stake on top such as a splint;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and the arrangement of a hot abscess, and cut out what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Il semble que nous ayons terminé la lecture de ce texte médical ancien. Voulez-vous continuer avec une autre partie du texte ? Ou bien est-ce pour une raison spécifique que vous avez mentionné "de la cuixe brisie" ?
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the hip is often broken, and one well knows it when it turns in front and behind;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is to bind it with a bandage above the wound, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on their face, then stretches each of their limbs to an equal length with theirs.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the breakage is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near to the root of the thigh, then it will be one of the tendons that goes towards the elbow, and the other tendons below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is close to the knee, and then have the bandages near the knee, and the extension downwards.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then place the mirrors to the bone equally in both hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then put the poultice and the bandage, so that an abscess does not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a warm abscess, let it subside and then return to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	the bandage is made in the same manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap above the wound with a thick double strap in two or three, and leave the superfluous parts, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the knee, and push the long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and let the end of the thread come up.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn to the leg and to the thigh the bandage; then put on the splint stars, and put a star on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then place the wooden wedge between the leg and the thigh of soft fabric to put it in equal tightening; then begin to tie strongly three or four turns on the splint.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go further up the splint, the tension will lessen.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two ends of the thread that you have put between the leg and the thigh, and tie three stars above, then go down to the lower part at the head of the thread as far as near the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and tighten it so that it does not move from its place; then leave it thus; and if there comes neither abscess nor swelling nor any other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, then dislodge it, and realign what has come out, as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are bone fragments that grasp, then it should be smoothed out, if one can.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then it must be split open, and the splinter drawn out.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and heal it as we have said, until it is sound.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the collarbone is broken, thus setting in place splints, as with the shoulder and arm.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	nevertheless, the restoration thus made does not creak out the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in one day, or a little more or less, according to the various constitutions of the patients.
de la ruelle dou genoil	De la rupture du genou.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that there is often a small break in the joint of the knee, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only by a crack or an incision, and there is great pain, and not little pain, and this seems quite severe.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that one sets equal those who are crooked to their axis, until they are assembled and can move.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and put a rounded splint on it, if you need one, and tighten it as is needed, then mend all the breaks that we have said to treat in other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar ones.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If one puts on every bandage which is necessary for him, until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of a break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, because one is called by right "tibia", and the other is called "fibula".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and there is every other breaking or fracture as it comes in the arm, and for that reason the restoration is just like that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns out of shape on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone (fibula) is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the big bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen well;
et torne desoz.	and it becomes swollen.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then make an extension, and put it in place, and bind the splints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but nevertheless, it is necessary if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, that the splint be shorter and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and apply according to your power.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints that encircle the leg from one end to the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee down.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap them in two places one bandage above and below, and bind it firmly in the middle also, and at that moment the leg cannot decline to the right or to the left, and thus it is well.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and if it is necessary to prevent the knee from bending too much, and it is of wood, and one places the leg to prevent movement, and thus it is properly done in the fracture where there is a wound.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, so as to see if there is an abscess or other accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if he cures it until they are healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of a break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle rarely breaks, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and crush, and there is no other injury than bruising in many cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	If it has a break in the bones of the foot and you see these bones jutting out one over the other, then have the patient put their foot on the ground, as if they were going to walk, and then place your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, and press them so that they return to their places.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then put on the plaster and bandages above, and under the patient's foot place a small wooden splint at two joints swollen, then hold it to the foot tightly, then when you have wrapped the cloth around, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then untie the bandage, for you will find that the bones are equalized, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there is any of the toes broken, repair them, just as we have said about the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put on the broken toe an arrowhead according to the length of the toe, and let it be a little thicker, then place under the foot that small wooden splint which I said, and hold it tightly.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three, or more, break them; and put a pin on each one as much as its quantity requires, wrapped in a linen cloth, and hold the table under the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let them be on the top of the head of the table outside the belly of the foot, so that they touch well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other breakages, when we have spoken;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and secure each accident as it is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of a break of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of the natural woman is broken, make her sit up and stretch it out, then incline her to the part of the back, and have her held from behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the natural belly of the patient with cotton, and put in it as big as I am.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then get the woman to stand up and lift her back a little bit at a time, and then the cotton will spring out, until it comes to the natural opening, and the bone will come back with the bulk.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when it wants to urinate, one removes the cotton, and when it has urinated, one puts it back in, and thus does it for seven days or so.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	if it will be restored the break, and if you see, take a bladder of thistles, and tie to the anus a cord, and put all the bladder in nature.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the cord firmly, until the bladder is blown out inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	nature will return the break.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be filled with cotton and let it like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the shoulder blade of man or woman is broken, so restore it thus as we have said in the hip bone.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these nearby breakages are not hidden from one who puts their study and skill into it, and hears my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture it signifies a return to the right path of restoration.
enten le donques.	then understand this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the penis, when it is fractured, take a goose gall and put it in the penis;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap it with cloth tightly around, and let it be so for three days or so on, and he will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or arm or similar, that he be healed immediately, so that the stitches which we have said may witness to.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals and an abscess forms, then close it with pitch, or if you have nothing else, then start to restore the break in that very same hour or day, so that pus does not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus comes out, then let the restoration alone for just nine days, until the abscess is calmed down, and do not touch it on the tenth day or the quarter, because you would bring about bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the skin's surface, it is necessary that you gently point it out with your fingers, making a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if you do not have the instrument extended to put even on your hands, then straighten it with this tool which is of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and its width is according to the size of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary for the surgeon to take three or four, according as he may need them in each cure of fracture.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be red and one pouch big, that it does not bend at all with the pressure on the member under your work, and it should be angled before, and thick in the middle forward, thus.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palainche", because it is necessary to put the curved bones on top of the visible bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and push it back once, as far as it will go, and have them be even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, it is necessary that you cut off the top of the bone, so that the instrument may have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, then cut off with a suitable instrument, such as a knife or saw, to your ability;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then reset the fragments that are remaining in the bone from sharpness and small shreds.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reduced and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you do so that it is in its place, then soak the bandage in black vinegar and properly bind it to stay in place.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put on the wound cerote or any other thing that would make oil ooze from it, lest it bring about infection and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer ointments when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the break.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times have done this the foolish physician, and have had brought over the patient either dead or corrupted sometimes;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and be the dislocations softer and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or great, and you doubt that a bad accident may come from it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then you must not put on poultices.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but envelop around, instead of poultices, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the bow is inflamed towards the wound, so remove what you have put on top of it in vinegar and put on a healing salve for wounds, such as tetrofarcation salve and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the member twice a day, morning and evening, until it is healed and cured.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be bound in such a way that the lower part bends slightly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days pass and it cannot heal but instead turns into a swelling, know that it has small bones, so you should sew the wound with thread, and remove all these loose pieces of bone that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess or some other manner of corruption comes to the place, so it behooves you that you treat it, according to what is said in its chapter before this.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and shows on the member, as the bone of the shin or of the shoulder, and other similar ones of the great members, do not pull it out, for many times death comes from this, but leave it until it rots.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	by chance it will come out through it after 20 days or 30, then heal the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot [do something], then let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	the blisters that come on the scab
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often come across after the breaking of the bone, especially when it is near the joint, and this thing is hard to see in the shape of the member.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance the limb may not be able to do its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Then pay attention if the nose is fresh.
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if the administrator gives medicines of astringent kind, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, aloe vera, and similar others, then take any one of these things or all together, and mix them with vinegar that is astringent or with almond milk or with oil.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put it on the nose in poultices, and tie it well, and do not loosen it for a day.
